# Tips
## Week3
  - **1. Master the "Augmentation" Approach to AI**

    Do not use ChatGPT to generate your work from scratch. Instead, write the skeleton or draft based on your own experience first. Then, use AI to critique it: ask it to identify gaps, logical flaws, or areas for strengthening. This ensures the output remains *yours* while leveraging AI for enhancement. Faculty can easily spot generic AI content, but they value critical analysis augmented by tools.

    **1. 掌握AI的“增强”用法**

    不要用ChatGPT从零开始生成你的作业。相反，先根据你自己的经验写出骨架或初稿。然后，用AI来批判它：让它找出缺漏、逻辑缺陷或需要加强的地方。这样既能保证产出是*你的*，又能利用AI进行提升。老师很容易识别出通篇由AI生成的内容，但他们看重经由工具辅助的批判性分析。

  - **2. Design Incentives for "One Level Higher"**

    When creating incentive structures, avoid the trap of purely individual metrics (which create silos) or purely group metrics (which allow free riders). The best practice, as seen in the Nucor case, is to pitch incentives to "one level and one level higher." For example, incentivize a manager based on their unit's performance *plus* the performance of the larger division. This forces collaboration and the sharing of best practices without sacrificing individual accountability.

    **2. 为“高一级”设计激励机制**

    在设计激励结构时，要避免纯粹的个人指标（会导致孤岛效应）或纯粹的集体指标（会导致搭便车）。正如Nucor案例所示，最佳实践是将激励锚定在“本级和高一级”。例如，对经理的激励应基于其部门的表现*加上*整个事业部的表现。这迫使大家在不牺牲个人责任感的前提下进行协作和分享最佳实践。

  - **3. Adopt the Mindset of a "Knowledge Worker"**

    Being a knowledge worker isn't just about having a degree; it is about **reflective learning**. After completing a task or a project, always step back and ask: "Could I have done this better? Did I do anything wrong? Is there a tool that would have improved my performance?" Differentiate yourself from a skilled worker by constantly analyzing your own process, not just executing tasks.

    **3. 树立“知识型工作者”的心态**

    成为知识型工作者不只是拥有学位，更在于**反思性学习**。在完成一项任务或项目后，永远要退一步问自己：“我能做得更好吗？我做错了什么吗？有没有工具能提升我的表现？”通过不断分析自己的工作流程而不仅仅是执行任务，让自己从普通技术工人中脱颖而出。

  - **4. Match Technology Readiness with Organizational Readiness**

    In technology transfer or implementation, "one size fits all" is a recipe for failure. Use the **Readiness Matrix**: Mature (High TRL) technologies can be plugged into any firm. However, conceptual (Low TRL) technologies generally result in failure if introduced to a firm with low "Demand Readiness" (no in-house R&D capability). Ensure the maturity of the solution matches the maturity of the recipient organization.

    **4. 将技术就绪度与组织就绪度相匹配**

    在技术转移或实施中，“一刀切”是导致失败的配方。使用**就绪度矩阵**：成熟（高TRL）的技术可以植入任何公司。然而，概念性（低TRL）技术如果被引入“需求就绪度”低（没有内部研发能力）的公司，通常会导致失败。确保解决方案的成熟度与接收组织的成熟度相匹配。

  - **5. Be Practical with Organizational Change**

    Don't blindly apply textbook theories to your workplace. If you are in an SME with limited resources, do not demand a dedicated "Foresighting Department"—you might get fired for being unrealistic. Instead, start small: look for blind spots, listen to customers, and identify weak signals. Context is king; adapt your strategies to the "bandwidth" and culture of your specific organization.

    **5. 对组织变革要务实**

    别把教科书理论盲目套用到职场上。如果你身处资源有限的中小企业，不要要求设立专门的“预见部门”——你可能会因为不切实际而被炒鱿鱼。相反，从小处着手：寻找盲点，倾听客户，识别微弱信号。背景为王；要根据你所在组织的具体“带宽”和文化来调整你的策略。
## Summary Week 4 Conceptual Models & Implementing Technology Intelligence
  - **The Theoretical Framework (Design, Direct, Develop)**

    The core of this week’s lecture focused on the theoretical underpinnings of setting up a Technology Intelligence (TI) system. We moved beyond *what* TI is to *how* to implement it from scratch. The process is governed by **TI Management**, which consists of three critical phases: **Designing** (creating a theoretical model suitable for the specific industry and organizational culture), **Directing** (orienting the system, allocating resources, and assigning analysts to fulfill the mission), and **Developing** (continuously monitoring and upgrading the system to ensure it doesn't fail). This management layer sits above the operational cycle of searching, filtering, and analyzing information.

    **理论框架（设计、指导、发展）**

    本周讲座的核心重点是建立技术情报（TI）系统的理论基础。我们从 TI *是*什么，转向了*如何*从头开始实施它。这个过程由 **TI 管理** 主导，包含三个关键阶段：**设计**（创建适合特定行业和组织文化的理论模型）、**指导**（以履行使命为导向调整系统、分配资源和指派分析师）以及 **发展**（持续监控和升级系统以确保其不会失败）。这一管理层位于搜索、过滤和分析信息的运作循环之上。

  - **The Great Debate: Intelligence \*of\* the Organization vs. Organizational Intelligence**

    We debated two distinct approaches to TI. **"Intelligence of the Organization"** refers to a top-down approach where decision-makers formulate specific questions ("When will this technology mature?") and direct analysts to find answers. This is efficient and focused but risks confirmation bias and myopia. Conversely, **"Organizational Intelligence"** is a bottom-up approach where every employee acts as a scout (the "passive" mode), gathering information and pushing it upward. While this fosters innovation (e.g., the Adobe/Xerox example) and diverse perspectives, it can lead to chaos and information overload ("noise") if not properly filtered through knowledge management systems.

    **大辩论：组织的智能 vs. 组织性智能**

    我们辩论了两种截然不同的 TI 方法。**“组织的智能（Intelligence of the Organization）”** 指的是自上而下的方法，决策者制定具体问题（“这项技术何时成熟？”）并指导分析师寻找答案。这很高效且聚焦，但有确认偏见和短视的风险。相反，**“组织性智能（Organizational Intelligence）”** 是一种自下而上的方法，每个员工都充当侦察员（“被动”模式），收集信息并向上推送。虽然这促进了创新（例如 Adobe/Xerox 的例子）和多样化的视角，但如果没有通过知识管理系统进行适当过滤，可能会导致混乱和信息过载（“噪音”）。

  - **Data Sources & The "Color" of Intelligence**

    The lecture categorized intelligence sources into three "colors": **White** (publicly available info like patents and publications), **Grey** (informal info from experts, conferences, and trade shows), and **Black** (illegal or unethical methods like dumpster diving, fake interviews, or supplier leaks). While Black intelligence exists in reality, the focus should be on ethical gathering. A crucial insight was that suppliers and "transit hubs" (like airports where experts gather) are often rich sources of Grey intelligence.

    **数据来源与情报的“颜色”**

    讲座将情报来源分为三种“颜色”：**白色**（公开信息，如专利和出版物）、**灰色**（来自专家、会议和贸易展的非正式信息）和 **黑色**（非法或不道德的手段，如翻垃圾桶、虚假面试或供应商泄密）。虽然黑色情报在现实中存在，但重点应放在合乎道德的收集上。一个重要的见解是，供应商和“中转枢纽”（如专家聚集的机场）通常是灰色情报的丰富来源。

  - **Organizational Structures (Lichtenthaler's Model)**

    We examined three structural modes for TI units:

    1. **Structured (Centralized):** A dedicated HQ unit with decentralized listening posts. Common in large, hierarchical organizations (e.g., Government agencies).
    2. **Informal (Decentralized):** Everyone participates; relies on culture, "slack resources" (free time for exploration), and job rotation. Common in SMEs or innovative tech firms (e.g., Google).
    3. **Hybrid:** A mix, such as forming ad-hoc "communities of practice" for specific technologies (e.g., combinatorial chemistry) that may later be integrated into the central unit.

    **组织结构（Lichtenthaler 模型）**

    我们审查了 TI 单元的三种结构模式：

    1. **结构化（集中式）：** 拥有专门的总部单元和分散的监听站。常见于大型等级制组织（如政府机构）。
    2. **非正式（分散式）：** 每个人都参与；依赖于文化、“松弛资源”（用于探索的空闲时间）和工作轮换。常见于中小企业或创新科技公司（如 Google）。
    3. **混合式：** 两者的混合，例如为特定技术（如组合化学）组建临时的“实践社区”，随后可能被整合进中央单元。

  - **The "Tool": Formulating the Right Questions**

    We introduced the **Kerr Information Needs Template**. The most critical step in TI is framing the right question using the 5W1H method (Who, What, Where, When, Why, How). The template helps stakeholders collaboratively define **Application Areas** (where can it be used?), **Technological Aspects** (feasibility, skills), and **Market/Commercial Aspects** (cost, ROI). A key addition to this canvas is considering **Ethics and Policy**, which are often overlooked but vital.

    **“工具”：制定正确的问题**

    我们介绍了 **Kerr 信息需求模板**。TI 中最关键的一步是使用 5W1H 方法（谁、什么、哪里、何时、为什么、如何）构建正确的问题。该模板帮助利益相关者协作定义 **应用领域**（可以用在哪里？）、**技术方面**（可行性、技能）和 **市场/商业方面**（成本、投资回报率）。这个画布的一个关键补充是考虑 **伦理和政策**，这两点经常被忽视但至关重要。
## Learning Tips & "Secret Recipes" for Assessment Week 4
  1. **Logbook Strategy: Aim for Level 4**

     - **Don't just summarize.** "Level 1" work is just repeating the lecture.
     - **To get an "A":** You must demonstrate **Higher-Order Thinking**.
       - *Context:* Relate the theory to your specific work experience.
       - *Critique:* Identify challenges or gaps in the theory based on reality.
       - *Solution:* Propose "out-of-the-box" mitigation strategies or improvements that go beyond the textbook.
     - **The "Secret Ingredient":** The professor explicitly stated that discussing **Ethical Implications** (which are often missing from standard frameworks) will "win his heart." Use this wisely in your logbook analysis.

     **Logbook 策略：以此为目标冲刺 Level 4**

     - **不要只是总结。** “Level 1” 的作业只是复述讲座。
     - **要拿“A”：** 你必须展示 **高阶思维**。
       - *背景：* 将理论与你的具体工作经验联系起来。
       - *批判：* 基于现实识别理论中的挑战或差距。
       - *解决方案：* 提出超越教科书的“跳出框框”的缓解策略或改进方案。
     - **“秘方”：** 教授明确表示，讨论 **伦理影响**（这通常在标准框架中缺失）会“赢得他的心”。在你的 Logbook 分析中明智地使用这一点。

  2. **The "Boring Paper" Assignment (Compulsory)**

     - **Task:** Read the paper by **Lichtenthaler** (provided in the reading list).
     - **Requirement:** You must create a **Visual Synthesis** (Mind Map, Block Diagram, or Pictorial representation) of the paper's key messages.
     - **Constraint:** Do not write a long essay about it. The goal is to act like an analyst: extract value from dense information and present it concisely. This is a *compulsory* entry for your final logbook submission.

     **“无聊论文”作业（必修）**

     - **任务：** 阅读 **Lichtenthaler** 的论文（在阅读清单中提供）。
     - **要求：** 你必须创建论文关键信息的 **视觉综合**（思维导图、框图或图形表示）。
     - **约束：** 不要写长篇大论。目标是像分析师一样行事：从密集的信息中提取价值并简洁地呈现。这是你最终 Logbook 提交中的一个 *必修* 条目。

  3. **Discussion Forum Etiquette**

     - **Avoid "Me Too" Comments:** Do not just agree with previous posts.
     - **Build & Twist:** Take an existing point (e.g., short-term vs. long-term) and add a specific, novel angle (e.g., "How does short-term thinking affect the retention of HR talent in a toxic culture?").
     - **Debate:** It is encouraged to respectfully counter-argue. If someone says "Top-down is best," argue for "Bottom-up" using specific examples of innovation or missed opportunities.

     **讨论论坛礼仪**

     - **避免“我也一样”的评论：** 不要只是同意之前的帖子。
     - **构建与转折：** 拿出一个现有的观点（例如，短期与长期），并增加一个具体的、新颖的角度（例如，“短期思维如何影响在有毒文化中保留 HR 人才？”）。
     - **辩论：** 鼓励尊重的反驳。如果有人说“自上而下最好”，请用创新的具体例子或错失的机会来为“自下而上”辩护。

  4. **Upcoming Schedule (Zoom)**

     - **Next Week:** Guest lecture by **Renee** (via Zoom) followed by the professor's lecture (also via Zoom). There will be no physical class.
     - **Action:** Look out for the Zoom link details by next Wednesday.

     **接下来的安排（Zoom）**

     - **下周：** **Renee** 的客座讲座（通过 Zoom），随后是教授的讲座（也通过 Zoom）。没有线下课。
     - **行动：** 留意下周三之前发出的 Zoom 链接详情。

# Lectures
## Week 1
  - **00:00 – 02:46: Introduction to Foresighting Tools and Reading Load**

    ...tons and tons of things. Read doesn't mean you have to understand everything and imbibe everything. You need to give a cursory look and get the bigger picture, and see what is the important aspect of it. If it's relevant, you note it down. And it's only later on you're going to dive deep into techniques. Okay? If you look at—many of you mentioned about forecasting—if you look at forecasting tools, there are dozens of tools, techniques, and analysis available. If you expect a module to teach you everything, no one can do justice. So, what I'm here to do is to expose you to different techniques, okay, and what are the advantages and disadvantages. If you think at some point, for example, I will talk about qualitative techniques, I'll talk about quantitative techniques. In qualitative techniques, there are a few which I will give you an idea of how it is done. The reason is when you are expected to do that particular one, you have to dive deep to do that particular one. Because not all techniques are suited for all kinds of scenarios. So, I'll give you the breadth of the knowledge, and then you have to pick it up along the way. That's what this module is. So, you'll have to read, as a foresighting officer, as an intelligence officer, you need to read tons and tons of boring, drowsy—trust me, I'll ensure that I'll give at least a couple of articles which will put you to sleep. Because when I read the module, I had to read it three, four times because every time I started off, it put me to sleep. But that is the dirty job of an intelligence officer. Okay? You need to look for what is called as "gray information." You need to look for white spaces. And to get those white spaces, you need to dig into articles and identify the gem from there. That's valuable for your organization because if you look for very obvious clues that are out there—like he said, right, "I read news articles to know what is happening in the industry." By the time it comes as news articles, what happens? If you are a company, they're going to pick signals from there. You're already too late. You're not going to win the race.

    ……成千上万的东西。阅读并不意味着你必须理解所有内容并全盘吸收。你需要粗略地浏览，了解大局，看看其中重要的方面是什么。如果相关，你就记下来。只有在后来你才会深入研究具体技术。好吗？如果你看——你们很多人提到了预测——如果你看预测工具，有几十种工具、技术和分析方法可用。如果你期望一个模块能教会你一切，那是无法做到的。所以，我在这里要做的是让你们接触不同的技术，好吗，以及它们的优缺点是什么。比如，我会谈论定性技术，我会谈论定量技术。在定性技术中，我会向你们介绍其中几种是如何操作的。原因是当你被期望使用某种特定技术时，你必须深入研究才能掌握它。因为并不是所有的技术都适合所有类型的场景。所以，我会给你们知识的广度，然后你们必须在过程中自己掌握它。这就是这门模块的内容。所以，作为一名预见官员，作为一名情报官员，你需要阅读成千上万无聊、令人昏昏欲睡的东西——相信我，我会确保给你们几篇会让你们睡着的文章。因为当我备课时，我不得不读了三四遍，因为每次我开始读的时候，它都让我睡着了。但这正是情报官员的苦差事。好吗？你需要寻找所谓的“灰色信息”。你需要寻找空白领域。为了找到那些空白领域，你需要深入挖掘文章并从中识别出精华。这对你的组织很有价值，因为如果你只寻找外面非常明显的线索——就像他说的，“我阅读新闻文章来了解行业发生了什么。”等到它成为新闻文章时，会发生什么？如果你是一家公司，竞争对手也会从那里获取信号。你已经太晚了。你赢不了这场比赛。

  - **02:46 – 05:32: The Three Types of Intelligence Information (White, Gray, Black)**

    So, the smartness lies in, before it becomes a news article, you become the news article. For that, you need to do the dirty job of digging into dirty paperworks, and sometimes, in intelligence, there is something called—there are three kinds of information. One is white, the other one is gray, the third one is black. White information are published informations like news articles, patents, publications, everything, right? And even products sometimes. Gray information are information that you collect from talking to experts. You're hand-collecting data, right? You talk to them, you ask them, "Hey, what do you think the industry will be five years down the line?" And many of the articles on foresighting that is written is as an outcome of talking to experts like that. Since you collect the data talking to experts, they are called gray information. And there is something called black. Which is... What is black information? What is black money? Something like that. What is black information?

    Student: Dirty money?

    Professor: Dirty money. Likewise, dirty information. How do you get it?

    Student: Illegal.

    Professor: Like what? Like how?

    Student: Insider trading.

    Professor: Insider trading... which is one possible ways. Some industries, especially in the pharmaceutical industry—I don't know if I've shared with MT5004 folks—what they do is, one chemical company, pharmaceutical company, they will look into the trash cans of their competitor company because there could be wealth in the trash can which they shred and put. They go dig in and find some information out of it. Sometimes they hijack people from one company to another, which is very frequently happening in tech companies. All these come under black information. If you want to be in the forefront of innovation—don't go and tell this professor is propagating something illegal, okay? But I'm just saying what is happening in the industry, right? So, if you want to be in the forefront of innovation, people look for all kinds of information, and you can't wait for neatly published thing and then go and look into it to make your company decision. That's not going to work. So, in the process of teaching you how nasty it is, I will also make you read some nasty articles. If you're not ready for it, good for me. Drop the module. Right?

    所以，聪明之处在于，在它成为新闻文章之前，你先成为新闻。为此，你需要做深入挖掘繁琐文件的苦差事，有时，在情报中，有三种信息。一种是白色，另一种是灰色，第三种是黑色。白色信息是公开的信息，如新闻文章、专利、出版物，所有这些，对吧？有时甚至包括产品。灰色信息是你通过与专家交谈收集的信息。你在手动收集数据，对吧？你和他们交谈，问他们，“嘿，你认为五年后的行业会是什么样？”许多关于预见性的文章都是与此类专家交谈的结果。因为数据是你通过与专家交谈收集的，所以它们被称为灰色信息。还有一种叫做黑色信息。那是……什么是黑色信息？什么是黑钱？类似那样的。什么是黑色信息？

    学生：脏钱？

    教授：脏钱。同样地，脏信息。你怎么得到它？

    学生：非法手段。

    教授：比如什么？怎么做？

    学生：内幕交易。

    教授：内幕交易……这是一种可能的方式。一些行业，特别是在制药行业——我不知道我是否与MT5004的同学分享过——他们做的是，一家化学公司或制药公司，会去翻竞争对手公司的垃圾桶，因为垃圾桶里可能有被粉碎掉的财富。他们去挖掘并从中找到一些信息。有时他们从一家公司挖角人才到另一家公司，这在科技公司经常发生。所有这些都属于黑色信息。如果你想处于创新的前沿——不要去说这个教授在宣传非法的东西，好吗？但我只是说行业中正在发生什么，对吧？所以，如果你想处于创新的前沿，人们会寻找各种信息，你不能等待整齐发表的东西，然后再去研究它来做公司决策。那是行不通的。所以，在教你们这行有多残酷的过程中，我也会让你们读一些枯燥的文章。如果你还没准备好，那对我很好。退课吧。对吧？

  - **05:32 – 08:20: Presentation Skills and Class Expectations**

    Then the second thing. When it comes to this module, I, as decision makers, you know that they are time-pressed. They are not going to read your 10 pages or 20 pages report. Whatever intelligence you gather, you should be able to summarize it in a neat pictorial form to them. One example is we already have in this... here. Big Data Analytics. This is a report created for decision makers which involved months and months of efforts. And every block out there will tell the decision makers who are the companies there, whom I know, whom I do not know, what kind of technologies are there, what kind of agencies are there that I need to tap into for my funding, and everything. So, every outcome as an intelligence officer, you need to present it in a very concise, pictorial form like this to your bosses. So that when they give a cursory look, they kind of get the bigger picture, and they want to dive deep into certain things, they will ask you and you will give tons of documents related to it later on. But your first presentation has to be like this. So, many of the presentations which you do for this module will not be in the form of write-up, blah, blah, blah. It will be in the form of giving in form of mind map, pictures, road map, whatever you can think of in pictorial form because that's going to train you to be an analyst at some point, right? Because you can't give... You need to have reports written down, but that you can anyway do. You have ChatGPT, blah, blah, blah, right? But what you need to do is present all the information. There are some homeworks wherein I'll give you to read an article which is very boring and take the gist of it and present it in this form as well. That will assess you on whether you're able to pick gems out of rubbish and then present it in a form that is palatable to the decision makers who are time-pressed. Make sense to you? If you think you're not up to it, again, drop the module. Okay? So, this is what you can expect from the module. You may have to read. You may have to present, be able to present. And I will have forum discussion. I don't take attendance for this module, unlike 5007. And I'll make the webcast available as well. If you're here, I want you to be here. You get what I mean?     然后是第二件事。说到这个模块，作为决策者，你们知道他们时间紧迫。他们不会读你的10页或20页报告。无论你收集什么情报，你都应该能够以整洁的图示形式向他们总结。这里就有一个例子：大数据分析（Big Data Analytics）。这是一份为决策者创建的报告，涉及数月的努力。那里的每一个区块都会告诉决策者那是谁的公司，我认识谁，我不认识谁，有什么样的技术，有什么样的机构是我需要利用来获取资金的，以及一切。所以，作为一名情报官员的每一个成果，你都需要像这样以非常简洁、图示的形式呈现给你的老板。这样当他们粗略一看，就能了解大局，而当他们想深入研究某些事情时，他们会问你，然后你再给他们成吨的相关文件。但你的第一次演示必须是这样的。所以，你们为这个模块做的许多演示不会是以书面形式，巴拉巴拉巴拉。它将是以思维导图、图片、路线图的形式，无论你能想到的什么图示形式，因为那将训练你成为一名分析师，对吧？因为你不能给……你需要有写下来的报告，但无论如何你都能做到。你有ChatGPT，巴拉巴拉，对吧？但你需要做的是呈现所有信息。会有一些作业，我会让你们读一篇非常无聊的文章，提取它的要点，并以这种形式呈现。那将评估你是否能够从垃圾中挑选宝石，然后以一种时间紧迫的决策者可以接受的形式呈现出来。这有道理吗？如果你认为你做不到，再次强调，退课。好吗？所以，这就是你可以从这个模块期待的。你可能需要阅读。你可能需要演示，能够演示。我会进行论坛讨论。我不像5007那样这门课点名。我也会提供网络直播。如果你人在这里，我希望你的心也在这里。你明白我的意思吗？参与课堂讨论。不要忙于你的Snapchat，巴拉巴拉。如果你在这里，就在这里。并参与很多小组活动，因为你不可避免地需要与小组合作。今天也是，我希望你们作为一个小组在一个话题上工作。你知道，在这个模块中，你将被迫像顾问一样思考和工作。会有很多小组活动。

  - **19:15 – 22:30: Hindsight, Insight, and Foresighting Explained**

    ...Five years down the line, ten years down the line. Bear in mind, for many of you who shared your ideas on why you are in this class, five years down the line, ten years down the line, when it comes to foresighting, you are not here to predict exactly "this is what is going to happen." If you were to do it, you're doing wrong foresight. Okay? Five years down the line, ten years down the line, future could be like this, or like this, or like this, or like this. You come up with or you paint different scenarios of the future. Right? And what you do today is, if one of those futures were to come into reality, how am I going to prepare myself to navigate through, rather than being thrown out of it. You get what I mean? So let's break it down to your personal life. Okay. Tomorrow if I ask you, what is your day going to be like, Karishma?

    Student: I'll do another module at the same time.

    Professor: You'll wake up and you whatever your day job is, you'll do and then you'll be here for the class. But if I ask you like a few months down the line, will you be able to say?

    Student: Not so accurately.

    Professor: Yeah. Especially if I ask you about your summer. In June, on June 15th, what are you going to do?

    Student: Oh, my mom has plans to go to India, while my father has plans to go to Europe.

    Professor: Whatever, right? If that were to happen, how do I prepare myself today? If this were to happen, what do I do? If I'm going to look for jobs, what do I do? So future... or foresighting is all about what could be potential future, what could be one of the potential states—or there could be multiple states—and how I prepare myself to be there if one of the states were to happen. Right? And when you do that, even that is data-based. Because if you were to paint this scenario could happen, that scenario could happen, you need to collect a lot of data as well. What kind of data you will collect? You'll collect data about... if you're looking for a job. What kind of data you will collect to paint your future scenarios?

    You might even look at which countries are doing well. You might even closely watch Trump, what he's doing, so that you can avoid him neatly and look for elsewhere, right? And you might look at how technology... what is AI happening, is it becoming a fad or is it there to disrupt you? There is... this is one question which is haunting many people. Is AI there to remain or leave? Right? Many questions are hovering around that. When it comes to energy system, he said solar. Is it solar the way that we need to go or is it something else? Is it already maturing or is it saturated? That's one question that we will be looking at. There are other promising energy... you know, alternative energy that you can bet on. Right? So you need to collect data on many aspects as well. Everything is data-based. Not one is not... Now you understand the difference?

    ……五年之后，十年之后。请记住，对于你们许多分享了为什么在这个课堂上的想法的人来说，五年之后，十年之后，当谈到预见时，你不是在这里准确预测“这就是将会发生的事情”。如果你那样做，你就是在做错误的预见。好吗？五年之后，十年之后，未来可能像这样，或者像那样，或者像这样，或者像那样。你想出或者你描绘未来的不同场景。对吧？而你今天做的是，如果那些未来中的一个成为现实，我将如何准备自己去驾驭它，而不是被甩出去。你明白我的意思吗？所以让我们把它分解到你的个人生活中。好的。如果明天我问你，Karishma，你的一天会是什么样？

  - **22:30 – 26:10: Evolution from Forecasting to Intelligence to Foresighting**

    In the earlier days, people only talked about forecasting. With whatever data they got, they tried to extrapolate for one, two years down the line. It was fine in older days because technology wasn't... or the environment wasn't... wasn't moving so fast, so dramatic. So forecasting was enough. And intelligence is something which many of the top-notch companies in innovation engage in. Because as soon as clues come, you change your business model. You change your customer... the way the customers... For example, right, when... when there was a time when people in the retail sector thought, okay, festive season, Chinese New Year is coming. Which means what? Stock up all your products because there is going to be huge sales, right? But it's not... over time they realized that it's not just festive means more sales, it is also festive season together with people's mindset. Right? If people are very uncertain about their jobs, though it's Chinese New Year, do you think they're going to spend more? Right? So it is not just about festive season, it's about broader socio-economic context also that plays a role in your business. So they started doing intelligent decisions in order to be more agile in the marketplace. That is intelligence. But then they realized all this is not enough, we need to think about... if you want to be in the forefront of innovation, you cannot be always reactive. Oh, this happened today, so I'm reacting to it. This happened today, I'm reacting to that. That cannot be the way if you want to be in the forefront of innovation. So what you do is you want to be the driver of the whole thing. Which means what? You want to see in the future what could be the potential things and then you want to take decisions today so that you are not taken by surprise. You're not thrown out of the business. That's what is foresighting. Yes, Moammar?

    Student: Um, just a query regarding all of this. What we are doing... we'll look at what technologies will be the future... or particular technologies... I mean, not particular technologies but what will be the future technology, but will we take a particular technology and look at how that... the future of that technology will be? For example, since I'm looking at solar, I'm looking at the past two years how the price has drastically dropped from where it was. So something like that also... a particular technology and how the forecast of that technology.

    Professor: There are different levels to foresighting. That's what you would have seen in Carlson's article as well. If you are working on one particular technology or if you are like her, R&D, making R&D decisions. For example, you are investing in solar, you are investing in wind or you are investing in geothermal, right? You want to... you have been investing in solar all along. And now you think, is this the right strategy or not? Then you dive deeper in solar, but you also look at competitor technology and analyze whether it's better for me to invest... continue investing here or invest there. So that is one level wherein within a business unit you are looking at this particular technology. That is one level. But foresighting spans different levels. As I said earlier, it could be a small R&D group, it could be an organization, it could be an industry, it could be a country. That's why this topic is applicable to all levels starting from individuals. That's why I said even if you don't apply the techniques for your company, all the techniques could be applied for the individual level as well, including Knowledge Management. Okay? So the focus can be different. The techniques that you learn will be applicable with cover breadth of it. Good question. Anything else?

    在早期，人们只谈论预测。用他们得到的任何数据，他们试图外推未来一两年。在过去那是可以的，因为技术没有……或者环境没有……没有移动得那么快，那么剧烈。所以预测就足够了。而情报是许多顶尖创新公司从事的事情。因为一旦线索出现，你就改变你的商业模式。你改变你的客户……客户的方式……例如，对吧，当……曾经有一段时间，零售行业的人认为，好的，节日季节，农历新年快到了。这意味着什么？囤积你所有的产品，因为将会有巨大的销售，对吧？但这不仅仅是……随着时间的推移，他们意识到不仅仅是节日意味着更多的销售，也是节日季节加上人们的心态。对吧？如果人们对他们的工作非常不确定，即使是农历新年，你认为他们会花更多钱吗？对吧？所以这不仅仅是关于节日季节，更广泛的社会经济背景也在你的业务中发挥作用。所以他们开始做智能决策，以便在市场上更加敏捷。那就是情报。但后来他们意识到所有这些是不够的，我们需要考虑……如果你想处于创新的前沿，你不能总是被动的。噢，今天发生了这件事，所以我对此做出反应。今天发生了这件事，我对此做出反应。如果你想处于创新的前沿，那不能是方式。所以你要做的是你想成为整件事的驱动者。这意味着什么？你想在未来看到什么可能是潜在的事情，然后你想在今天做出决定，这样你就不会措手不及。你不会被踢出局。那就是预见。是的，Moammar？

    学生：嗯，只是关于所有这些的一个疑问。我们在做的……我们会看什么技术将是未来……或者特定技术……我是说，不是特定技术而是什么是未来技术，但我们会拿一个特定技术来看看那个……那个技术的未来会怎样吗？例如，因为我在看太阳能，我在看过去两年价格是如何从原来的水平急剧下降的。所以类似那样的……一个特定技术以及那个技术的预测。

    教授：预见有不同的层次。这也是你在Carlson的文章中会看到的。如果你在致力于某一项特定技术，或者如果你像她一样，研发，做研发决策。例如，你在投资太阳能，你在投资风能或者你在投资地热能，对吧？你想……你一直都在投资太阳能。现在你想，这是正确的策略吗？然后你深入研究太阳能，但你也看竞争对手的技术并分析对我来说是更好投资……继续在这里投资还是在那里投资。所以那是一个层次，在一个业务单元内你看这个特定的技术。那是一个层次。但预见跨越不同的层次。正如我之前说的，它可以是一个小的研发小组，它可以是一个组织，它可以是一个行业，它可以是一个国家。这就是为什么这个话题适用于从个人开始的所有层次。这就是为什么我说即使你不为你的公司应用这些技术，所有的技术也可以应用于个人层次，包括知识管理。好吗？所以重点可以是不同的。你学习的技术将适用并涵盖它的广度。好问题。还有别的吗？

    Professor: Right. They play an important role. Yes. So in a nutshell, what they say is foresighting is all about carrying out a process. I want you to bear in mind. Foresighting is not about telling "this is what you can expect in future." Foresighting is about a process which enables a firm to be prepared for one of the possible futures. And how do you do it? This is how you do it. It is a structured process which involves many people. And it is aligned with the strategy of the company because what happens is, in a company, first the decision makers should think and value foresighting. In many organizations, it doesn't happen. They think, okay, we are running the show, what's a big deal? We are fine. They move on. Only to realize that something is coming as a shock to hit them. Okay, many companies, organizations unfortunately run that way, especially small and medium enterprises. They are worried about their current bread and butter. You can't expect them to be futuristic. That is why Singapore is very good in the sense they are expecting A*STAR and all to handhold these SMEs to say, "Hey, they cannot think about their future. You help them to prepare them for future." They conduct and handhold, run a workshop saying, "You're working in this, but future is there, you'll be thrown out of business, so try to change." And they do lot of programs to support them. If you're in a large organization, you have the luxury to engage in foresighting but not many bosses understand the value of it. We'll talk more about it in future. Because they think it is like wasting time. Trust me, you know, many of the foresighting activity and processes and workshops happen in a resort, in a spa, in a cool environment. Bringing in people. And they look at it as cost to the organization. They look at it... nothing tangible comes out of it. What is the KPI? What have you met? If they keep asking this question, you cannot exactly show.   - **35:20 – 38:00: The Power Zone and Workshop Methodology**

    So what you need to do is, the boss has to agree this is important, and engage in the process of calling people from diverse background, have a facilitator to moderate it who commands respect, and then goes through workshop. There are two workshops that Carlson's article mentions. And there are many tools like technology space matrix, the power zone centroid, everything. All these tools, trust me, I was working with a colleague for wind turbine on solar... you know, competitor, in laying out forecasting foresighting for them, and all we did was simple Excel sheet. You don't need fancy tools. You don't need large database and run analysis. Sometimes it is just a question of having simple Excel sheet, having a proper template of what you want, seeking opinion and analyzing it. That's good enough. And if you look at technology space matrix and all, these are all very subjective. Companies use different tools and techniques. That's why I said if I were to teach certain tools... if I were to spend all my energy today teaching about the the different tools used in Carlson's article, it's a waste of your time and my time. Because today it is this, tomorrow when you join a company they are going to use a different tool or you are going to devise a different one which is context specific for the company. So don't waste your time on tools going by... When I give you article, don't waste your time on understanding all the tools and techniques because you should be aware that such a tool exists. That's enough for this module. Okay, there is something called this, this is how it's broadly done. That's about it. Don't break your head on it. Okay? That's where you want to extrapolate the article. Look at what is more important than wasting your time in nitty-gritty details. Don't do that. You cannot afford to do that in technology intelligence unless you are doing the analysis job. An analyst? Yes, they need to worry about it. Okay? Now, what you need to do is as a boss and as you have called in a facilitator, you create an environment for people to come and meet, and they always start from where they are, what they are. That's where the power zone comes. What is that which defines me today? What are my core strengths? What are my capabilities? What are my assets? Okay? And then you this is also out of workshop, right? Because different people think the firm is defined as certain thing in different ways. For you, you might think you know this module is big good because it helps me in analyzing tools. He might think it's because it helps me in decision making, right? Different people have difference. That's why you come together to define what is my core. That's where the bosses also play a role with the strategic vision. Then once they define the current state... okay, if you look at me, me as a faculty, here I am, I'm a tenured professor at NUS, I'm good with teaching, my research and my services. That's me as my... the three pillars that I have. Right? Then at the end of the workshop, you carve out a nice neat question of where you want to go. Because if you were to be futuristic with an open-ended question, it's endless. Right? So that's where the bosses try to define or frame a question which is going to be the anchoring point...

    所以你需要做的是，老板必须同意这很重要，并参与召集来自不同背景的人的过程，让一位受人尊敬的引导者来主持，然后通过研讨会。Carlson的文章提到了两个研讨会。还有很多工具，如技术空间矩阵（technology space matrix）、力量区质心（power zone centroid）等等。所有这些工具，相信我，我和一位同事为风力涡轮机关于太阳能……你知道，竞争对手，为他们制定预测预见，我们所做的只是简单的Excel表格。你不需要花哨的工具。你不需要大型数据库和运行分析。有时这只是一个拥有简单Excel表格，拥有你想要的适当模板，寻求意见并分析它的问题。这就足够了。如果你看技术空间矩阵等等，这些都是非常主观的。公司使用不同的工具和技术。这就是为什么我说如果我要教某些工具……如果我今天要花所有的精力教关于Carlson文章中使用的不同工具，那是浪费你的时间和我的时间。因为今天它是这个，明天当你加入一家公司时，他们会使用不同的工具，或者你要设计一个针对公司具体情况的不同工具。所以不要把时间浪费在工具上……当我给你文章时，不要把时间浪费在理解所有的工具和技术上，因为你应该知道这种工具存在。这就足够这个模块了。好的，有这种东西，这是大概怎么做的。大概就是这样。不要在这上面伤脑筋。好吗？那是你想要外推文章的地方。看看什么比把时间浪费在细枝末节上更重要。不要那样做。除非你在做分析工作，否则你在技术情报中承担不起那样做。分析师？是的，他们需要担心这个。好吗？现在，你需要做的是作为老板，并且你已经叫来了一位引导者，你为人们创造一个环境来见面，他们总是从他们在哪里，他们是什么开始。这就是力量区（power zone）出现的地方。什么是今天定义我的东西？我的核心优势是什么？我的能力是什么？我的资产是什么？好吗？然后你这也是出于研讨会，对吧？因为不同的人认为公司以不同的方式被定义为某种东西。对于你，你可能认为你知道这个模块很好因为它帮助我分析工具。他可能认为这是因为它帮助我做决策，对吧？不同的人有差异。这就是为什么你们聚在一起来定义什么是我的核心。这就是老板们通过战略愿景也发挥作用的地方。然后一旦他们定义了当前状态……好的，如果你看我，我作为一个教员，我在这里，我是NUS的终身教授，我擅长教学，我的研究和我的服务。那是作为我的……我拥有的三个支柱。对吧？然后在研讨会结束时，你精心设计一个你想去哪里的漂亮简洁的问题。因为如果你要用一个开放式问题来展望未来，那是无止境的。对吧？所以这就是老板们试图定义或构建一个将成为锚点的问题的地方……

  - **38:00 - 39:29: Defining the Framework for Foresight**

    ...for that team to think about foresight. For example, this question will be: I have been betting on solar technology. Does it make sense for me to invest more in this as a company, or should I not? That could be a question for this company. For me, I have been doing teaching, research, and service as a tenured professor in NUS. Is it okay to continue in this trajectory, or is AI going to disrupt the whole industry so much that I need to completely revamp my skill set? That could be a framing question for me.

    So, at the end of the first workshop, you need to, as bosses, you need to define what is the framework which is going to define your foresight. If you leave it open-ended saying, "I want to be competitive five years down the line," it's too vague. Right? Or it could be what many of you mentioned about AI: Is AI going to disrupt my industry [such] that I need to quickly revamp my workforce on AI-related tools and techniques? That could be a broad question. Or is it a fad for my industry?

    ……讓那個團隊去思考前瞻性（Foresight）。例如，這個問題可能是：我一直押注於太陽能技術。作為一家公司，我是否有意義繼續在此投入更多資金，還是不應該？這可能是這家公司的一個問題。對我來說：作為新加坡國立大學（NUS）的終身教授，我一直從事教學、研究和服務工作。繼續沿著這個軌跡發展是可以的嗎？還是說人工智慧（AI）會徹底顛覆整個行業，以至於我需要完全重塑我的技能組合？這可能是我的一個框架性問題。

    因此，在第一次研討會結束時，作為老闆，你們需要定義將用來界定你們前瞻性工作的框架是什麼。如果你們留一個開放式的結尾，說“我想在五年後保持競爭力”，這太模糊了。對吧？或者它可以是你們許多人提到的關於 AI 的問題：AI 是否會顛覆我的行業，以至於我需要快速讓我的員工掌握 AI 相關的工具和技術？這可能是一個廣泛的問題。或者這對我的行業來說只是一時的熱潮？

And trust me, many groups will come up with the answer saying, "In 2032, there are going to be more AIs, there are going to be hologram professors, blah blah blah, AI bots, chatbots as teaching assistants, etc." Trust me, that's not called foresighting. If you were to take that to Prof Tan, he is going to throw it back at you.

    那我們做一件事，我們先休息一下，然後進行這個課堂活動。課堂活動……希望那時候你們都已經組好隊了。對於這個模組，我們一組大約五到六名成員。你們不必為了這個小組項目而堅持跟同一組人在一起。當然，小組項目是有的，你們必須有一個小組，但今天你們可以隨意組隊。看看你們是否與組員有協同效應。所以組成一個五到六人的小組，我希望你們在休息後進行這個活動。

    請記住我說過的話：前瞻（Foresighting）是一個過程。它不是預測。過去，在我提供所有這些背景知識之前，我讓學生做過這個活動。相信我，許多小組會給出的答案是：“在 2032 年，會有更多的 AI，會有全息影像教授，等等等等，AI 機器人，聊天機器人助教等等。”相信我，那不叫前瞻。如果你們把那個拿給 Tan 教授看，他會把它扔回給你們。

    所以，你們需要明白前瞻是一個過程。而且我也告訴過你們，前瞻是關於描繪未來的場景，為此你們需要收集數據。你們會收集什麼樣的數據？你們將採取什麼樣的過程？這將是你們小組活動的重點。清楚了嗎？不要告訴我教室的最終結果，這不是我想要的。我希望你們展示如果 Tan 教授要回答這個問題，他該如何進行情報活動。這就是我希望你們關注的重點。大家清楚了嗎？所有人？我們在短暫休息後開始。我們 7:35 回來。然後我們會快速做完這個，接著我們會繼續……好的。

    **Professor**: Very good question. Power zone is your current capability. Dynamic capability is how you evolve your capability over time. So power zone is a static snapshot of what you are good at today. Dynamic capability is the process of changing that power zone. Very good question. We will cover dynamic capabilities later in the module. It's a very important concept in strategic management. But for now, just think of power zone as your current strength. What are you good at today? What pays your bills today? That's your power zone. Okay?

    **教授**: ...识别新机会。所以我可以增强它，或者我可以扩展它。比如说，我只做技术管理的研究。也许我应该把它扩展到知识管理。或者也许我应该把它扩展到开放式创新。或者也许我应该把它扩展到可持续性。那是对我权力区域的扩展。或者是全新的机会。我不再当教授，我去当企业家。我把我的研究转化为一家初创公司。对我来说那是全新的机会。而那个决定是我基于预见练习做出的。这就是文章所说的。

    大家都清楚了吗？这三个结果？这三个结果非常重要。为什么？你们认为为什么识别这三个结果很重要？为什么我不能只说，好吧，我想做什么就做什么？

    **学生**: [关于资源/方向的回答听不清]

    **教授**: 正是。为了分配资源。如果我想开一家公司，我需要不同种类的资源。如果我想把我的研究扩展到可持续性，我需要雇佣可持续性方面的专家，或者我需要与可持续性领域的人合作。所以资源分配取决于这三个结果。这就是为什么你需要非常清楚你想要实现什么。

    **教授**: 正确。

    **学生**: [关于动态能力的问题听不清]

    **教授**: 很好的问题。权力区域是你目前的能力。动态能力是你如何随着时间演变你的能力。所以权力区域是你今天擅长什么的静态快照。动态能力是改变那个权力区域的过程。很好的问题。我们稍后会在模块中涵盖动态能力。它是战略管理中一个非常重要的概念。但现在，只把权力区域想成是你目前的优势。你今天擅长什么？今天什么为你支付账单？那就是你的权力区域。好吗？

  - **01:22:45 - 01:25:06: Intelligence vs. Foresight**

    **Professor**: Okay. So let's move on. We talked about foresight. Now let's talk about intelligence. What is intelligence? How is it different from foresight? Or are they the same?

    **Student**: [Inaudible answer]

    **Professor**: Okay. Intelligence is about information. Foresight is about future scenarios. Okay. Anybody else?

    **Student**: [Inaudible answer about actionable insights]

    **Professor**: Actionable insights. Very good. Intelligence leads to actionable insights. Foresight leads to future scenarios. But aren't future scenarios actionable? If I say in 2032 classrooms will be like this, isn't that actionable? I can start building that classroom today.

    **Student**: [Inaudible answer]

    **Professor**: Okay. So let's look at the definition. Intelligence warns an organization of technological threats and identifies potential technological opportunities. It's about managing technologies, present and emerging, from both inside and outside the company. It's like a radar. You're constantly scanning. Scanning for what? Threats and opportunities.

    And it transforms gathered information into intelligence. So information is just raw data. Intelligence is processed data that is useful for decision making. That's the key difference. Information is everywhere. Google gives you information. But Google doesn't give you intelligence. You have to process that information, put it in context, analyze it, and then it becomes intelligence.

    Is this clear? The difference between data, information, and intelligence?

    Data is raw numbers. Information is data with context. Intelligence is information with analysis and implications.

    So, for example, if I say the temperature is 30 degrees. That's data. If I say the temperature is 30 degrees, it's hot today. That's information. If I say the temperature is 30 degrees, it's hot today, so people will buy more ice cream, so I should stock up on ice cream. That's intelligence.

    You see the difference? It leads to action. Decision making.

    And foresight... foresight is about looking further ahead. Intelligence is usually about the here and now, or the near future. Foresight is about the long term. Five years, ten years, twenty years. And it involves more uncertainty. Intelligence tries to reduce uncertainty. Foresight embraces uncertainty. It says, okay, there are multiple futures. I don't know which one will happen, but I can prepare for all of them. Or I can try to shape the future I want.

    So they are related, but they are distinct. Intelligence feeds into foresight. You need good intelligence to do good foresight. But foresight goes beyond intelligence. It adds imagination, creativity, scenario planning.

    Okay? So that's the key distinction.

    **教授**: 好的。那我们继续。我们谈论了预见。现在我们来谈谈情报。什么是情报？它与预见有何不同？还是说它们是一样的？

    **学生**: [回答听不清]

    **教授**: 好的。情报是关于信息。预见是关于未来情景。好的。还有其他人吗？

    **学生**: [关于可操作见解的回答听不清]

    **教授**: 可操作的见解。非常好。情报导致可操作的见解。预见导致未来情景。但是未来情景不是可操作的吗？如果我说 2032 年教室会是这样，那不是可操作的吗？我今天就可以开始建造那个教室。

    **学生**: [回答听不清]

    **教授**: 好的。那我们来看看定义。情报警告组织技术威胁并识别潜在的技术机会。它是关于管理技术，现在的和新兴的，来自公司内部和外部。它就像雷达。你在不断扫描。扫描什么？威胁和机会。

    并且它将收集到的信息转化为情报。所以信息只是原始数据。情报是经过处理的、对决策有用的数据。那是关键区别。信息无处不在。谷歌给你信息。但谷歌不给你情报。你必须处理那些信息，把它放在背景中，分析它，然后它才变成情报。

    清楚了吗？数据、信息和情报之间的区别？

    数据是原始数字。信息是带有背景的数据。情报是带有分析和含义的信息。

    所以，例如，如果我说气温是 30 度。那是数据。如果我说气温是 30 度，今天很热。那是信息。如果我说气温是 30 度，今天很热，所以人们会买更多冰淇淋，所以我应该储备冰淇淋。那是情报。

    你看到区别了吗？它导致行动。决策。

    而预见... 预见是关于看得更远。情报通常是关于此时此地，或不久的将来。预见是关于长期。五年，十年，二十年。并且它涉及更多不确定性。情报试图减少不确定性。预见拥抱不确定性。它说，好的，有多种未来。我不知道哪一种会发生，但我可以为所有这些做准备。或者我可以试图塑造我想要的未来。

    所以它们是相关的，但它们是不同的。情报输入到预见中。你需要好的情报来做好的预见。但预见超越了情报。它增加了想象力、创造力、情景规划。

    好吗？所以那是关键区别。

    So next week, we will have a guest lecture. Mr. Koo Seng Meng from AI Singapore. He will talk about "Technology Intelligence: Why & Practice". He will share his experience from AI Singapore, how they do intelligence, why it is important for them. It will be a very interesting session. I encourage you all to come prepared with questions.

    And also, please form your groups for the class activity. You can start discussing the "NUS in 2032" topic. We will do the activity next week after the guest lecture. So come prepared with some initial thoughts.

    And also, please go through the reading materials for next week. It will help you understand the guest lecture better.

    Okay? Any final questions?

    **Student**: [Inaudible question about group size]

    **Professor**: Five to six members. Yeah. Five to six members per group.

    **Student**: [Inaudible question]

    **Professor**: Yes, you can. You can have members from different backgrounds. That's actually better. Diverse perspectives.

    Okay. If no more questions, thank you all. Have a good evening. See you next week.

    **教授**: ...今天的讲座就到这里。我知道这对大家来说是漫长的一天。但我希望你们觉得这节课有用。至少对这个模块是关于什么的，什么是预见，什么是情报有了一个初步了解。

    下周，我们将有一场客座讲座。来自新加坡人工智能（AI Singapore）的 Koo Seng Meng 先生。他将谈论“技术情报：原因与实践”。他将分享他在新加坡人工智能的经验，他们如何做情报，为什么这对他们很重要。这将是一个非常有趣的会议。我鼓励大家准备好问题。

    另外，请为课堂活动组建你们的小组。你们可以开始讨论“2032 年的新加坡国立大学”这个话题。我们将在下周客座讲座后进行这个活动。所以请带着一些初步的想法来。

    还有，请阅读下周的阅读材料。这将帮助你们更好地理解客座讲座。

    好吗？还有最后的问题吗？

    **学生**: [关于小组规模的问题听不清]

    **教授**: 五到六名成员。是的。每组五到六名成员。

    **学生**: [问题听不清]

    **教授**: 是的，你可以。你可以有来自不同背景的成员。那实际上更好。多样化的视角。

## Week 2
  [18:05–18:07] **Class setup, participation rules, and agenda**
  **English** Today we’ll do it a bit differently so there’s more synergy within each group. It will be a group challenge rather than purely individual work. If your group genuinely feels there are free-riders, let me know. Likewise, if someone clearly explored the topic much more deeply and became a key contributor, tell me as well—so they can receive extra points.
  For today’s agenda: we’ll start with a quick summary of last week, then we’ll have our guest segment, and finally we’ll discuss technology intelligence and foresighting—especially *why it is important*. That “why” is what the benchmarking report is mainly about.

  **Chinese** 今天我们换一种方式，让小组内部更有“协同感”。会更像小组挑战，而不只是个人输出。
  如果你们小组确实觉得有人在“搭便车”，可以私下告诉我；反过来，如果有人明显做得更深入、贡献更关键，也请告诉我，我会给额外加分。
  今天流程是：先快速回顾上周内容 → 然后是嘉宾分享 → 最后讨论技术情报（TI）与远见/前瞻（foresighting），重点是：**为什么它重要**。这也是今天 benchmarking report 的核心。

  [18:06–18:07] **Last week recap prompt + forum posting guidance**
  **English** Any questions from last week—what foresighting is, and Carlson’s article? I noticed there were quite a few non-ChatGPT discussion posts on the forum, which is good. But there was also a strange random post under the “ChatGPT” area and I couldn’t identify who posted it.
  Also, the number of posts has gone down (that’s fine). I’m not opening new posts for this week; the forum activity will continue until next week. Please contribute more, but focus on quality.
  One more point: I didn’t set up the Canvas page for people to post figures. If you have a block diagram or mind map, can you post it on Canvas? Then I’ll go back to checking the forum for both ChatGPT and non-ChatGPT discussions. If you have any difficulties with the module, raise them early—don’t wait until the end of the semester.

  **Chinese** 上周内容有没有问题？比如：什么是 foresighting，以及 Carlson 那篇文章？
  我看到论坛里有不少“非 ChatGPT”的讨论贴，挺好。但也出现了一个很奇怪的“ChatGPT 区”的随机贴，我找不到是谁发的。
  另外，这周帖子数量下降也没关系。我这周不会再开新的讨论区，论坛讨论会延续到下周。请继续发，但更强调**质量**。
  还有：我之前没在 Canvas 上专门开“图表/框图/思维导图”的提交位置。如果你做了框图或 mind map，可以发在 Canvas 上。之后我会同时看论坛里 ChatGPT 和非 ChatGPT 的内容。
  课程有任何困难请尽早说，别拖到学期末才反馈。

  [18:07–18:09] **Quick conceptual check: foresighting vs crisis management**
  **English** Let’s answer a few quick questions. First: is foresighting the same as crisis management?
  No. Crisis management is about solving immediate, pressing problems. It’s reactive. Foresighting is long-term and proactive: you’re dealing with future-oriented problems, mitigating threats *and* identifying opportunities. Crisis management is usually about mitigating threats in the short term, not about opening up future opportunities.

  **Chinese** 我们先用几个问题做“概念校准”。第一个：foresighting 是不是等同于 crisis management（危机管理）？
  不是。危机管理解决的是**眼前的紧急问题**，偏被动、反应式；foresighting 面向**更长期**，偏主动：既要降低未来威胁，也要抓住未来机会。危机管理通常只关注短期“止损”，而不是系统性布局机会。

  [18:09–18:11] **Is TI/foresight purely “technology”? + broader lenses including ethics**
  **English** Next: is technology intelligence and foresighting purely a “technology-only” exercise? If you Google “technology intelligence,” you’ll also see competitor intelligence, social intelligence, etc.
  The answer is: it used to be narrower when time horizons were short and the scope was limited. But when the time horizon becomes longer, you must look beyond technology: market, social factors, environmental factors, and human behavior. (Think back to the classroom-of-the-future exercise—learning behavior matters.)
  And one more lens that many people forget: ethics. Ethics should be part and parcel of technology assessment—especially in AI. Many of you working on AI will have encountered AI ethics; it matters at the system and societal level, and it needs to be included in how we assess and steer technology.

  **Chinese** 下一个问题：技术情报/前瞻是不是纯粹“只看技术”的事情？
  以前在**时间跨度短、范围窄**时，可能更像只看技术。但只要时间跨度拉长，你必须把视角扩展到：市场、社会、环境、人的行为等。（比如你们做“未来课堂”的活动，本质上就离不开学习行为。）
  另外一个经常被忽略的维度：**伦理**。伦理不应该缺席技术评估，尤其是 AI。做 AI 的同学基本都接触过 AI ethics——它会影响技术能不能被接受、能不能规模化落地，所以应该进入评估框架。

  [18:11–18:14] **Top-down vision vs structured process (Delphi)**
  **English** Another question raised on the forum: is foresighting basically a visionary leader giving directions—top-down speculation?
  A visionary leader can help, and foresight can be triggered top-down or bottom-up. But foresighting is fundamentally a *process* involving people with different skills and perspectives (R&D, business unit managers, etc.).
  If it’s only one leader driving it, it may work only if that person is unusually accurate—which is rare. If the leader leaves, the system can collapse. Worse, if that leader is strongly opinionated but wrong, the company gets locked into the wrong direction. This often happens in SMEs where the leader decides because they lack bandwidth.
  That does not mean “ignore visionaries.” In fact, foresight has methods like the **Delphi method**: systematically collecting opinions from *multiple* experts/leaders, iterating toward areas of consensus, and combining qualitative and quantitative evidence—rather than letting a single person dictate the future.

  **Chinese** 论坛里还有一个常见误解：foresighting 是不是“有个远见型领导拍板”，纯自上而下的推演？
  领导的远见当然重要，foresight 也可以自上而下启动，或者自下而上从一线发现信号。但本质上它是一个**流程**：要把不同角色（研发、业务单元、市场等）的视角整合起来。
  如果完全靠一个人带方向，只有在这个人极其“天才且持续正确”时才可能成功，但这很少见；领导离开后体系可能断掉；更糟的是领导如果强势但判断错，公司会被锁死在错误方向。中小企业确实常这样运行，因为资源不足。
  但这不等于不要专家/远见者。相反，foresight 里有 **Delphi 方法**：让多个专家/行业领导分轮次给判断、不断收敛共识，并结合定量与定性证据，而不是“一言堂”。

  [18:14–18:15] **Where ethics fits in foresight**
  **English** How does ethics come in? One way is as a guiding principle: it supports transparency and legitimacy, and clarifies what values the organization wants to advance.
  At what stage should ethics appear—early, mid, late? Ideally, it should be introduced early enough to define “what we are moving toward” and what is out of bounds. Detailed assessment can be refined later, but shared ethical direction prevents teams from optimizing toward a future that becomes unacceptable or non-adoptable.

  **Chinese** 伦理在 foresight 里怎么“落位”？一种很实用的理解是：伦理是一套**指导原则**，帮助透明化、建立合法性/可信度，并明确组织想坚持的价值。
  伦理应该在早期、中期还是后期出现？比较好的做法是：**早期就要出现**，先明确“我们想走向哪里、什么不能做”。后续可以再做更细的评估与审计，但如果一开始价值边界不清，团队很容易把系统优化到一个“社会不接受/难以落地”的方向。

  [18:15–18:17] **Transition to guest lecture**
  **English** Let’s welcome our guest speaker, Mr. Koo Seng Meng (AI Singapore). He has a busy schedule of travel and work, yet he still made time to join us.

  **Chinese** 接下来欢迎我们的嘉宾：AI Singapore 的 Koo Seng Meng 先生。行程很满，但还是抽时间来给我们分享。

  [18:17–18:20] **Guest background + key framing: real-world foresight is messy**
  **English** (Guest) I started with R&D and patents (e.g., early display technologies—many of you may not have seen cathode ray tubes). I moved from R&D into business development and technology portfolio work. In 2012 I joined Singapore’s public service (then under the Infocomm Development Authority).
  Over time I see myself as an “intrapreneur,” launching several first-in-region or first-in-world products across industry (e.g., Sony Ericsson, Siemens, and public sector roles). Today I’m Director of Talent Development at AI Singapore, working on capacity/capability building and shaping the talent ecosystem with government agencies.
  For today, I want to share AI Singapore’s ~8-year journey. In practice, technology forecasting/foresight is not clean-cut—it is messy. Often we understand things in hindsight more clearly than in real time.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）我最早做研发与专利（例如早期显示技术——现在很多同学可能都没见过阴极射线管 CRT）。后来从研发转到业务拓展与技术组合管理。2012 年进入新加坡公共部门（当时在 IDA 体系内）。
  我把自己看作“企业内创业者（intrapreneur）”，曾推动过一些区域首创/全球首创的产品与项目。现在我在 AI Singapore 做人才发展负责人，主要做能力建设、生态建设，并和政府机构一起塑造人才体系。
  今天我想用 AI Singapore 过去大约 8 年的发展过程来讲：现实世界里的预测/前瞻并不“干净”，往往很“混乱”；很多时候我们是事后回看才更清晰。

  [18:20–18:23] **AISG origin: national foresight cycle and phased national strategy**
  **English** (Guest) AI Singapore started in 2017, but the decision to invest in AI was discussed earlier (around 2015) at the national level under Singapore’s research governance structure. The key issue was: AI is a frontier technology, we “don’t know what we don’t know,” so we must invest strategically.
  AI Singapore was set up as a national program office coordinated across multiple government agencies. Early mandate: explore possibilities and “fail fast” if needed. By 2019 we learned what worked and what didn’t, helping shape Singapore’s National AI Strategy (version 1). In 2023 the strategy was updated to 2.0 as AI matured—from “what is AI?” to “what can we do with AI?”
  In the public sector we often behave like “professional crystal-ball users”: we ingest information (patents, industry conversations, signals), filter, analyze, spin up programs, and learn via feedback loops. That is forecasting/foresight at a national scale.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）AI Singapore 在 2017 年成立，但国家层面对 AI 的战略投资讨论更早（大约 2015 年）。核心难点是：AI 属于前沿技术，我们“不知道自己不知道什么”，所以必须更有策略地投。
  AI Singapore 被设为国家级项目办公室，由多个政府机构共同协调。早期使命很明确：探索可能性，必要时快速试错。到 2019 年积累了经验，推动形成国家 AI 战略 1.0；到 2023 年升级为 2.0——因为 AI 更成熟了，重点从“AI 是什么”转到“AI 能做什么”。
  公共部门很多时候像“职业水晶球”：我们尽可能多地收集信息（专利、产业访谈等），筛选分析，启动项目，再通过反馈回路不断调整——这就是国家尺度的 forecasting/foresight。

  [18:23–18:26] **AISG KPIs and “value chain” view of AI**
  **English** (Guest) Early KPIs were simple: publish 100 top AI papers, do 100 industry projects, and run “AI Grand Challenges” in key ministries/sectors (e.g., health, urban solutions, education). Over time, strategies evolve as the technology evolves.
  A useful way to see AISG is a pipeline from research → technology → governance → product innovation → talent development. Another lens is “value capture”: AI is just technology unless you can extract value—economic growth, research excellence, and talent outcomes. So we consider AI value across research, policy/platform, business, and talent pipeline.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）早期 KPI 很直白：顶级论文数量、产业项目数量、以及在关键领域做国家级挑战（比如医疗、城市、教育）。但随着技术发展，战略也必须调整。
  看 AISG 可以用“价值链/管线”的视角：研究 → 技术 → 治理 → 产品创新 → 人才发展。
  也可以用“价值获取”的视角：AI 如果不能带来价值（经济增长、科研能力、人才结果），就只是技术。所以我们把价值分布在研究、政策/平台、产业价值、人才管线等维度去管理。

  [18:26–18:30] **Innovation intermediary + Triple Helix + TRL and “valley of death”**
  **English** (Guest) In research terms, AI Singapore is a **public innovation intermediary**. A classical model here is the **Triple Helix**: government + academia + industry working together. Why? Industry often prefers technology at higher maturity (lower risk). Frontier know-how sits in universities, which is why tech transfer offices exist. Government underwrites experimentation risk, and an intermediary entity helps connect performers (research) with adopters (industry).
  We can think in **Technology Readiness Levels (TRL 1–9)**: early concepts (TRL 1–3), mature everyday products (TRL 7–9), and the hard middle (TRL 4–6) often called the “valley/chasm of death” where many technologies fail to cross into deployable products.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）用学术概念说，AI Singapore 属于**公共创新中介（public innovation intermediary）**。经典框架是 **三螺旋（Triple Helix）**：政府 + 学术 + 产业协同。原因很现实：企业通常更偏好成熟度高、风险小的技术；前沿知识更多在大学，所以需要技术转移；政府的角色是为试验与探索“兜底”，中介组织负责把“技术生产者/研究者”和“技术采用者/企业”连接起来。
  这里也会用 **TRL（技术成熟度等级 1–9）** 来理解：1–3 是概念与原理验证，7–9 是产品化与规模化，中间 4–6 是最难跨越的“死亡之谷”，大量技术就在这里卡住。

  [18:31–18:36] **AI-specific adoption challenge: model is small part; need MLOps + data engineering**
  **English** (Guest) In early AISG industry projects (around 2017), even with professors and researchers involved, outcomes often weren’t usable by companies. Back then, today’s cloud model ecosystems didn’t exist in the same way; many solutions were hard-coded or heavily fine-tuned. Models that looked good in development could break in production because real data differs and drifts.
  We learned AI adoption has specific challenges. Research and media hype often overstate adoption; real adoption and value realization can be much lower. One core reason: training a model is only a small part of an AI project. Real-world systems require integration into a digital platform, with two major capabilities many teams lack: **data engineering** and **MLOps (ML/LLM operations)**—deployment, monitoring, and managing model drift. Companies that succeed at AI often already run large-scale data/platform backends (cloud-scale operations).
  Key “proof point”: if the model never goes into production, no real-world value is created. That forced AISG to pivot: build internal engineering capability to translate research into deployable systems and feed insights back into policy and ecosystem diffusion.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）AISG 早期做产业项目时（2017 前后），即使有教授和研究者参与，结果也经常“不好用/落不了地”。当时的云生态和今天不一样，很多方案是硬编码或重度微调；一旦进入生产环境，真实数据分布不同、会漂移，模型就容易崩。
  我们发现 AI 的采用有“特有难题”。媒体的热度和真实落地往往不一致，真正能产生价值的比例可能很低。关键原因之一是：**训练模型只是很小一部分**。现实系统需要集成到数字平台，还需要很多团队缺乏的能力：**数据工程** + **MLOps/LLMOps**（部署、监控、漂移管理）。能把 AI 做成规模化能力的公司，往往本身就有大型数据平台/云化运营能力。
  一个非常硬的结论是：模型不上生产，就没有价值。所以 AISG 后来必须“转向”：补齐工程化能力，做研究到落地的翻译引擎，同时把一线经验反哺政策与生态扩散。

  [18:37–18:41] **Programs: readiness index + apprenticeship as capacity building**
  **English** (Guest) We shaped the ecosystem by diagnosing which organizations are ready. We built an **AI Readiness Index** (a short questionnaire) to classify organizations: AI-unaware → AI-aware → AI-ready → AI-competent. That helps target limited funding: some firms should first become aware; some should buy off-the-shelf solutions; some are ready for custom projects; and some are already competent and don’t need grants.
  For capacity building, we run the **AI Apprenticeship Programme**: working professionals join for ~9 months, train on real industry projects, and graduate with real deployment experience. Entry includes technical tests similar to major tech hiring styles—because industry evaluates practical ability, not only degrees.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）我们做生态建设时，一个关键动作是“先诊断组织是否准备好”。所以做了 **AI Readiness Index**（短问卷），把组织分成：AI 不认知 → AI 有认知 → AI 准备好 → AI 能胜任。这样才能把有限资金用在刀刃上：有的企业先去“补认知”，有的适合买现成方案，有的适合做定制项目，有的已经很强就不需要再拿补助。
  能力建设方面，有 **AI Apprenticeship Programme**：在职人士参加约 9 个月，用真实产业项目训练，最后带着“真实部署经验”出去。入选要做技术测试，形式接近大厂面试，因为行业更看重现场解决问题能力，而不只是学历。

  [18:41–18:45] **What makes an industry-ready AI engineer + “do AI” vs “do things with AI”**
  **English** (Guest) A strong industry AI engineer isn’t defined only by a computer science background. Many industry problems are domain-heavy (healthcare, aviation, logistics, creative industries). What matters is the ability to understand what data is needed and what “good problem framing” looks like in that domain.
  The labor market increasingly needs people who can *do things with AI*, not only people who can *invent AI algorithms*. We also standardize project delivery with agile approaches and package institutional knowledge into playbooks and tools so others can replicate it.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）行业里“好用的 AI 工程师”不一定只靠纯计算机背景。大量项目是强领域属性的（医疗、航空、物流、创意等），关键能力是：懂业务问题怎么定义、需要什么数据、数据质量风险在哪里。
  现在市场越来越需要“会用 AI 做事的人”，而不仅是“会发明算法的人”。同时我们用敏捷方式标准化交付，并把机构经验沉淀成手册/工具，让生态可以复制。

  [18:45–18:55] **Talent pipeline + GenAI shock + job exposure framing**
  **English** (Guest) Talent development must be intergenerational: we need to influence education one to two generations ahead. We built training hubs and progressively expanded from working professionals to schools, in collaboration with the Ministry of Education.
  After late 2022, generative AI accelerated automation. The key change is not “AI replaces humans” in a simple sense, but that AI-assisted digital automation scales rapidly, disrupting tasks and job scopes. Some analyses (e.g., industry reports and surveys) estimate a significant share of modern job tasks are automatable. A helpful framing is exposure: tasks can be insulated (low exposure), augmented (complementary), or disrupted (high substitution).
  Counterintuitively, some high-cognition creative work may be augmented rather than eliminated—because productivity increases (e.g., faster generation of concept variants), even if the workflow changes.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）人才发展必须看“代际”：至少要提前影响 1–2 代人的教育体系。我们先做成人/在职培训的资源库，再逐步往学校推进，并和教育部门合作。
  2022 年底之后，生成式 AI 让自动化加速。关键不是简单的“AI 取代人”，而是 **AI 辅助的数字自动化规模化**，从而改变任务结构与岗位内容。很多报告用“岗位任务可自动化比例”来描述冲击。
  比较实用的框架是“暴露度”：有的工作几乎不受影响（insulated），有的会被增强（augmented，互补），有的会被强替代（disrupted）。
  有趣的是，一些高认知的创意工作不一定被消灭，反而可能被增强——因为工具让产能上升（比如更快生成多版本概念方案），但工作方式会改变。

  [18:55–19:01] **Institutionalization: playbooks, regional LLM (Sea Lion), standards, and “human element”**
  **English** (Guest) As a public entity, long-term value is to encapsulate institutional knowledge and diffuse it—so we encode practices into handbooks/playbooks (how to start an AI project, what is or isn’t an AI project).
  We also invest in a regional language model initiative (Sea Lion) to better represent ASEAN contexts and reduce risks of cultural misrepresentation when models become dominant information interfaces.
  On “rewarding good actors,” standards matter. Singapore participates in ISO/IEC JTC 1/SC 42 (AI standards). Standards form a knowledge map and can support compliance and trust-building across jurisdictions.
  Finally, across all programs, the human element remains central: even if technology has clear advantages, individuals may resist adoption. Change management and mindset shifts are often decisive.

  **Chinese** （嘉宾）作为公共机构，长期价值在于把经验“制度化”并扩散出去，所以我们把方法写进手册/工具包（如何启动 AI 项目、什么算 AI 项目、什么不算）。
  我们也投入区域语言模型（Sea Lion），让模型更能覆盖 ASEAN 语境，降低“文化被错误代表”的风险——因为大模型越来越可能成为信息入口。
  对于“奖励守规矩的好参与者”，标准体系很重要。新加坡参与 ISO/IEC JTC 1/SC 42（AI 标准委员会），标准本身构成一张知识地图，有助于跨地区的合规与信任。
  最后，无论做多少技术项目，“人”的因素都绕不开：技术再好也可能有人抵触使用，所以变革管理与心态迁移往往是成败关键。

  [19:47–19:50] **From guest lecture back to benchmarking: the “luxury to think about the future” problem**
  **English** Let’s come back to a key tension raised in both the guest talk and the benchmarking report. Many firms say: *we are overwhelmed by current problems; we don’t have the luxury to think about the future*.
  This is the million-dollar question: how do you balance today’s survival with future investment? The report highlights that most businesses naturally focus on immediate operational issues and short-term returns, which crowds out foresighting.

  **Chinese** 回到一个在嘉宾分享和 benchmarking 报告中都反复出现的张力：很多企业会说——我们眼前问题已经够多了，根本没有“余力”去想未来。
  这正是“百万美元问题”：如何在**生存压力**和**未来投入**之间取得平衡？报告指出，大多数企业会被短期问题和短期回报牵着走，结果就是 foresighting 被不断挤压。

  [19:48–19:55] **SMEs, limited capability, and the role of intermediaries/government**
  **English** This challenge is especially real for small and medium enterprises. If you’re fighting for bread and butter today, asking you to plan five years ahead feels unrealistic.
  So what should such firms do? One option is to rely on intermediaries and government bodies. That’s precisely why innovation intermediaries exist. When industry is not ready to place bets on discontinuous technologies, the state often steps in early—setting up programs, grants, and shared infrastructure.
  Singapore is often described as being “creature-like” in sensing future threats early. Agencies step in to help SMEs gear up for transitions (for example, emissions-free futures in maritime industries). Firms with capability should juggle short-term and long-term internally; those without should leverage external support.

  **Chinese** 这个问题对中小企业尤其现实：如果今天都在为现金流和生存发愁，让你去想五年、十年后的未来，确实不现实。
  那怎么办？一种可行路径就是**借助中介组织和政府机构**。这正是创新中介存在的意义：当产业还没准备好为“断裂式技术”下注时，国家先行介入，通过项目、补贴、公共平台降低试错成本。
  新加坡常被形容为“提前感知风险”的国家。政府部门会帮助中小企业为转型做准备（比如航运业的减排转型）。有能力的大企业要内部平衡短期与长期；能力不足的中小企业则要善用外部资源。

  [19:55–19:58] **Link to benchmarking report: why profitability and market value**
  **English** This links directly to the benchmarking report. The report uses two outcome variables—**profitability** and **market capitalization**. Why these two?
  Because firms can fail in two opposite ways:

  * Focus only on current profits and lose the future.
  * Focus only on the future and lose current viability.
    The report classifies firms into four types (e.g., vigilant, vulnerable, neurotic, etc.) to show that balance matters. Over-optimizing either side is risky. Incentives and KPIs must reflect this balance.

  **Chinese** 这正好呼应 benchmarking 报告里的核心设计：为什么用 **盈利能力（profitability）** 和 **市值（market capitalization）** 这两个结果变量？
  因为企业可能在两个方向上失败：

  * 只看当下利润，未来被淘汰；
  * 只押未来，眼前先“饿死”。
    报告用四种企业类型（如 vigilant、vulnerable、neurotic 等）来说明：关键在于**平衡**。激励机制和 KPI 设计必须体现这一点。

  [19:58–20:01] **Adoption reality: POCs, employees, and change management**
  **English** A student shared a practical observation: many AI projects stop at proof-of-concept. At management level, expectations are high; at employee level, adoption is low because it adds workload and disrupts routines.
  This is common. Even in universities or public systems, people stop using tools when systems change too frequently. Without investment in **change management**, adoption will stall. Technology foresight without organizational change capability rarely translates into value.

  **Chinese** 有同学分享了很真实的现象：很多 AI 项目卡在 POC 阶段。管理层期待很高，但员工层面的采用率很低，因为工具增加了负担、打乱了原有流程。
  这种情况非常普遍。系统更新太快，人自然会放弃使用。如果企业不投入**变革管理（change management）**，再好的技术也难以落地。没有组织能力支撑的 foresight，很难真正创造价值。

  [20:03–20:06] **Framing the guest lecture as foresight value**
  **English** Bringing it back: the guest lecture answers the question, *how does a nation prepare for future technological disruption?*
  Key takeaways include: using readiness assessments, talent pipelines from school to workforce, and playbooks built from repeated experimentation (e.g., “100 experiments”). These are concrete ways foresight translates into value—not just abstract thinking.

  **Chinese** 回到主题：嘉宾分享本质上回答了一个问题——**国家如何为未来的技术颠覆做准备？**
  关键启示包括：用 readiness 评估工具、从学校到职场的人才管线、以及通过大量实验沉淀成“可复制的 playbook”（例如 100 次实验）。这些都是 foresight 转化为价值的具体机制，而不只是抽象讨论。

  **Professor:** Don't invest in change management and they want things to change, it's not going to happen. They should be aware of it. It's a big topic in itself. I'll see if I can cover a little bit of it in knowledge management. We need to move on. You have any pressing question? Yes.

  **学生：** 因为他提到中小型企业的信心问题……他们无法跨越鸿沟去接触 AI Singapore（新加坡人工智能计划），或者接触政府机构或部门。但因为他们的资源和财务状况有限，所以没有足够的资金。如果政府向他们收费……

  **教授：** 不，不，那是错的。政府会给这些公司提供补贴。这也取决于政府。所以你应该了解所有这些拨款。有一篇论文完全专注于各国提供的所有拨款，特别是针对不同国家的中小型企业，我们会看看那个。

  **学生：** 但是政府不能帮助所有这类公司，所以其中一些……

  **教授：** 他们需要有选择性，对吧？就像 Seng Meng 说的那样。他们会看这些公司的 AI 就绪程度（AI readiness）。如果还没准备好，他们会说：“去充实自己吧。”如果你有一点准备，他们会试着以此引导你。如果你已经准备得很充分了，他们会说：“再见。”因为你已经可以自给自足了。

  **学生：** 那么如果不被政府选中，我就得去找代理机构吗？如果我没有那么多钱做这种……

  **教授：** 你很快就会被吞并（cannibalized）。你需要为自己的未来至少投资一点点。如果你愿意投入一点，政府也会投入它的那部分。明白吗？

  **教授：** 好了。既然如此，我们继续讲课。天哪。好的。这是关于基准报告的第一个问题。

  **02:45 - 06:10: Introduction to Foresight Benchmarking Report**

  **Professor:** Regarding Seng Meng's thing on the top, right? How nation prepares for future or technological disruptions. How it equips... that's the whole message from this talk. How companies like you can tap into such resources and can tap into things like AI readiness levels, can tap into all those charts that he showed. Those are key valuable lessons for you. They didn't even leave the school; they are preparing them also that you need to be aware of.

  **Professor:** So it's more on foresighting at the national level that he shared, but there are lots of lessons for firms. Especially the most valuable being the AI Playbook. These agencies having done 100 experiments... he didn't elaborate more because this is one project wherein I was closely working with him. Which means the government decided, "I am going to help 100 companies in Singapore implement AI and show the returns." You see? This is where it ties up to today's topic. How foresighting is of value. What is the value of foresighting?

  **Professor:** So he mentioned in the initial days the foresighting was all about KPIs. How many companies you help? How many apprentices you created and all? That was the first two cycle. In the third cycle, that's when I started working with him on another project, it talks about what did AI Singapore achieve for the nation? What economic returns did they bring in? That's where the "100E" experiments were helpful. How much of revenue they created? How much of new products they developed? How many new markets they tapped into? So those are economic returns.

  **Professor:** So at some point, even at the national level, it's not enough if you just look at the earlier KPIs. You should also look at tangible value. And that's what any CEOs would ask you. If you say, "Can I implement foresighting for the company? Can you allocate some budget?" They might give you initially, but after the first two cycles they will ask you, "How did you create value for me, for my company?" And that's where the Foresight Benchmarking Report neatly fits in. It will be asked by bosses, it will be asked by country, it will be asked by industry as well.

  **教授：** 关于 Seng Meng 之前讲的内容，对吧？国家如何为未来或技术颠覆做准备。它是如何装备……这是那场讲座的核心信息。像你们这样的公司如何利用这些资源，如何利用像 AI 就绪水平这样的东西，利用他展示的所有那些图表。这些对你们来说都是非常宝贵的经验。最后但同样重要的是人才。国家如何从学校到职场培养人才。他们甚至还没离开学校，国家就已经在为他们做准备了，这也是你们需要知道的。

  **教授：** 所以他分享的更多是国家层面的前瞻（foresighting），但对企业来说也有很多教训。尤其是最有价值的 AI Playbook（人工智能行动指南）。这些机构做了100个实验……他没有详细说明，因为这是一个我和他密切合作的项目。这意味着政府决定：“我要帮助新加坡的100家公司实施人工智能并展示回报。”你看？这就是它与今天主题的联系所在。前瞻的价值是什么？前瞻有什么价值？

  **教授：** 他提到在早期，前瞻主要关于 KPI（关键绩效指标）。你帮助了多少家公司？你培养了多少学徒等等？那是前两个周期。在第三个周期，也就是我开始和他合作另一个项目的时候，讨论的是 AI Singapore 为国家取得了什么成就？他们带来了什么经济回报？这就是“100E”实验有用的地方。他们创造了多少收入？开发了多少新产品？进入了多少新市场？这些都是经济回报。

  **教授：** 所以在某种程度上，即使在国家层面，仅仅看早期的 KPI 是不够的。你还应该看有形的价值。这也是任何 CEO 会问你的。如果你说：“我可以为公司实施前瞻吗？你能分配一些预算吗？”他们最初可能会给你，但在前两个周期之后，他们会问你：“你为我、为我的公司创造了什么价值？”这就是《前瞻基准报告》（Foresight Benchmarking Report）恰好切入的地方。老板会问，国家会问，行业也会问。

  **教授：** 好的。请继续，我在听。

  **08:30 - 10:00: Evaluating Foresight Readiness vs. Performance**

  **Student:** Uh, as a decision maker, I think... I'm aware that there is a measurement that can give me advice what my organization or my company is standing on. Whether the foresighting for my company is enough or not. Which brings... which brings my company is dangerous in the future or is safe. So...

And then after that I categorize whether the company is at what stage before I make the decision of whether I should invest money.

  **Professor:** Yeah. So very good. Before I decide on whether I want to invest on foresighting itself, what is the need for my industry? Is it even needed? So that I don't become neurotic. Right? Yeah. What else?

  **Student:** So in order to do that, I think as a decision maker, one would definitely know how the company perform. So this measuring the firm performance would be one important criteria to know. So that then you will come to know whether you need the foresighting. So it's more of the firm performance.

  **Professor:** That cannot be the right gauge. So when you say performance what will you look at?

  **Student:** You look at the company performance, also your competitor, the data and things like that.

  **Professor:** But what if they are doing well today? So can they be satisfied about it? That's where the problem lies. I am good today but am I prepared for future? It's a question mark.

  **Student:** But if we don't know where are we performing today, then how do we...

  **Professor:** It's a hygiene factor. I don't deny it. Of course any boss will do that. Am I performing well or not? But you shouldn't use that as a metric to decide whether is my foresighting enough or not. That's what I mean. Of course we should be aware of performance. We should gauge it. We should know where they are standing with respect to competitors. But that, while that is hygiene factor, that cannot determine whether they should invest in futuristic vision or not. These two can be very different. That's why I said there are two things. When you look at performance, if you are looking at only profitability, that cannot be the right gauge. That's the whole crux of the article. You need to look at future potential of the company. That's where the market capitalization comes in picture. Let's take there and come here.

  **教授：** 是的。非常好。在我决定是否要投资于前瞻本身之前，我的行业对此有什么需求？是否真的需要？这样我就不会变得“神经质”（neurotic）。对吧？是的。还有什么？

  **22:30 - 25:00: Avoiding Confounding Factors & Industry Clustering**

  **Professor:** How did they manage to do? As an analyst if you can't do it, you're failed already. At least in this paper that's the simplest that they can do which they did.   **Class:** No.

  **Student:** How to...

  **Professor:** Usually they'll do the experiment like control one...

  **Professor:** Control and experimental sample is what they would do. That's what I did in my research next week which I'll show. Which happened in my case.

  **Professor:** So what they did is they looked at companies from different industries. Okay? They grouped them. And then they look at for this industry, what is the foresighting need? Okay? For... it will be different for different industries. And for each firms in each of those industries, they classify the firms maturity, foresighting maturity level. And then they classify the firms into four different types. So that will be done across different industries. Okay?

  **Professor:** So now they look at performance. Whether they perform... the those in foresight ready are doing well or not. And then they do an average across different industries. It is not fool proof but that's the first step towards avoiding confounding factors. You get what I mean?

  **教授：** 他们是如何做到的？作为一名分析师，如果你做不到这一点，你就已经失败了。至少在这篇论文中，这是他们能做的最简单的方法，他们也做到了。[Chang Wom] 做了更复杂的因果模型，我知道。有人知道吗？他们是怎么做到的？作为一名分析师，如果你做不到这一点，你就已经失败了。

  **学生：** 有人吗？

  **学生：** 他们的未来准备度（future preparedness）概念，即一致地使用成熟度和……

  **教授：** 确实如此。因为不同的行业需要不同的前瞻要求，成熟度也会不同。所以他们提出了这种聚类（clustering）：公司的成熟度水平是多少？所需的需求是什么？它们是持平的，还是神经质的，或者是处于危险之中，或者你知道，所有那些脆弱的情况。然后他们评估绩效。将成熟度与绩效进行比较。然后他们说：“是的，为未来做好准备的公司确实表现得更好。”

  **教授：** 如果你要分类和聚……大家都明白了吗？像这样的聚类有助于避免混淆因素影响结果。那是他们做的最简单的事情。清楚了吗？还是不清楚？

  **全班：** 不清楚。

  **学生：** 怎么……

  **教授：** 通常他们会做像控制组那样的实验……

  **教授：** 控制样本和实验样本是他们通常会做的。这正是我下周要在我的研究中展示的。但在这个案例中，因为他们是在收集过去的数据，你知道，他们在看为未来做好的准备以及之后的未来，他们做的是，即使你要做控制组和实验组，如果结果被来自不同行业的不同公司混淆了怎么办？这在我的案例中发生过。

  **教授：** 所以他们做的是，他们观察了来自不同行业的公司。好吗？他们将它们分组。然后他们看对于这个行业，前瞻需求是什么？好吗？对于……不同行业会有所不同。对于这些行业中的每一家公司，他们对公司的成熟度、前瞻成熟度水平进行分类。然后他们将公司分为四种不同类型。所以这将在不同行业之间进行。好吗？

  **教授：** 那么现在他们看绩效。他们是否表现……那些做好前瞻准备的是否表现良好。然后他们在不同行业之间取平均值。这不是万无一失的（fool proof），但这确实是避免混淆因素的第一步。你明白我的意思吗？

  **32:45 - 35:00: Technology Radar: From Signals to Strategy**

  **Professor:** Good thinking. But you need to know how this, the Radar, is coined. Anybody who has seen Radar before? This Radar, Technology Radar, actually originated from Cisco, the company. Anyone has done it? Okay. Radar is a powerful... I'll maybe, since you are not aware, I'll have a class on Radar itself. But Radar goes through all the three steps that are mentioned out here: the perceiving and prospecting. It basically... what it does is, in Radar, you scan the environment. Like what happened in Carlson's article, the second step. Go and scan the environment for information. And once you scan the environment, you start analyzing for what are the strong signals, what are the weak signals. And what are worth investing, what are not worth investing.

  If some things you feel as a group is worth investing further, you are going to probe into them. Invest money. "Oh, this, for example, AI is going to kill me down the line. So let me park certain portion of my budget into AI so that tomorrow I'm not going to be killed. I am ready kind of." If certain things you don't get clear signals... like for Blockchain, you feel like, "I don't know whether I should invest in." What you do is you start monitoring them.

  So based on the scan signals that comes in, you try to prioritize your R&D strategy into different buckets. Some are of immediate value, some are of long-term value, and some are of very futuristic one. Okay? Very futuristic one... maybe you are not bidding today, but it can come and kill you later. So you want to monitor it to see *when* I need to invest in it.

  Immediate one: high importance. Go put it there so that you are not being killed. Moderate one: they are not of that great importance. So what I'll do is I'll have a class to tell you how the Cisco Radar is all about. And what is more interesting is all the technology intelligence process that you undertake is a powerful communication tool.

  **Chinese Translation**

  **教授：** 很好的思考。但你需要知道这个“雷达”是如何构思出来的。有人以前见过雷达吗？这个雷达，技术雷达，实际上源自思科（Cisco）这家公司。有人做过吗？好吧。雷达是一个强大的……也许，既然你们不了解，我会专门上一节关于雷达的课。但雷达经历了这里提到的所有三个步骤：感知和展望。基本上……它所做的是，在雷达中，你扫描环境。就像卡尔森（Carlson）文章中提到的第二步。去扫描环境以获取信息。一旦你扫描了环境，你就开始分析哪些是强信号，哪些是弱信号。哪些值得投资，哪些不值得投资。

  如果作为一个团队，你们觉得某些东西值得进一步投资，你们就会去探索它们。投入资金。“噢，例如，人工智能（AI）将来会扼杀我。所以我要把一部分预算投入到 AI 中，这样明天我就不会被淘汰。我已经做好了某种准备。”如果某些事情你没有得到明确的信号……比如区块链，你觉得，“我不知道是否应该投资。”你要做的就是开始监控它们。

  因此，基于进入的扫描信号，你试图将你的研发策略按优先级分入不同的桶中。有些具有即时价值，有些具有长期价值，还有一些是非常未来导向的。好吗？非常未来导向的……也许你今天不押注，但它以后可能会来扼杀你。所以你要监控它，看看我*何时*需要投资它。

  即时的：高度重要。去把它放在那里，这样你就不会被淘汰。中等的：它们没那么重要。所以我将上一节课告诉你们思科雷达是怎么回事。更有趣的是，你们进行的所有技术情报过程都是一个强大的沟通工具。

  **35:00 - 37:00: Interpreting the Radar: Projects and Strategic Choices**

  **Professor:** If you were to present the Radar of your company, it will showcase all the... you know, the blocks and triangles that you see, they are nothing but projects of a firm. And the projects are split into whether they are radical, like what she said, incremental... whether they have immediate business potential or long-term business potential... how important they are... and how close they are. This is the TRL level that Seng Meng was mentioning. Some are market-ready projects and some are very basic projects.

  And in just a look at this Radar, you know if your company is being currently profitable as well as futuristic or not. Because if they haven't invested anything in the peripheral, which means they are not being futuristic. Right? And it could be a strategic choice of company saying, "I don't want to invest in anything basic. I am very applied in nature because I care about bread and butter." Okay. If it is a strategic choice, it's okay. Then you cannot expect to be in the forefront of innovation if you have projects only in this one... in this part. Right?

  So as a company, you will know where you stand in terms of whether your projects are only here or are there. Are they all radical in nature? Which means radical projects will take a long time for you to fetch money, but it can fetch a lot of money. Are you happy with that? Some companies decide to do that. Especially those working on rare diseases in biopharma industry. It takes a long time, right? Or blockbuster drugs, right? It takes a long time sometimes, but it fetches you a lot of money.

  **Chinese Translation**

  **教授：** 如果你要展示你公司的雷达，它将展示所有的……你知道，你看到的那些方块和三角形，它们不过是一家公司的项目。这些项目被分为是激进的（就像她说的），还是渐进的……它们是具有即时商业潜力还是长期商业潜力……它们有多重要……以及它们有多接近。这就是 Seng Meng 提到的技术就绪指数（TRL）水平。有些是市场就绪的项目，有些是非常基础的项目。

  仅仅看一眼这个雷达，你就知道你的公司目前是既盈利又面向未来，还是并非如此。因为如果他们没有在边缘领域投资任何东西，这意味着他们没有面向未来。对吧？这可能是公司的一种战略选择，说：“我不想投资任何基础的东西。我本质上非常注重应用，因为我关心的是生计（面包和黄油）。”好吧。如果是战略选择，那没问题。那么，如果你的项目只在这个……在这个部分，你就不能指望处于创新的前沿。对吧？

  所以作为一家公司，你会知道自己的立场，即你的项目是只在这里还是在那里。它们本质上都是激进的吗？这意味着激进的项目需要很长时间才能为你带来资金，但它可以带来很多资金。你对此满意吗？有些公司决定这样做。特别是那些在生物制药行业研究罕见疾病的公司。这需要很长时间，对吧？或者重磅炸弹药物，对吧？有时这需要很长时间，但它会为你带来很多钱。

  This is the last slide. So what can small companies do if they cannot do foresighting? They look at at least their past blind spot where they have failed so that they don't repeat the mistake.
