    但这些是你需要留意的事情，对吧？不仅仅是在国家层面，因为国家层面的事情最终变得更加可见一点，因为人们在谈论它，这里那里都在增加。那么你就可以把它描绘出来。预见过程是什么样的，他们经历了什么过程，等等。好的。

    现在。有一个画布，一个工具可以帮助构建问题。我不写成千上万的文章。第一件事是举办一个研讨会并拿出来……实际上这个特定的研讨会和框架或工具，在预见和情报中，我们总是称这种东西为 **工具（Tool）**。这个工具可以帮助提出正确的问题。这也简化了随后的搜索、过滤、分析过程。所以我们休息一下再看这个工具。好的，我们休息大概 10 分钟够了吗。最晚 40 分回来，但尽量在 35 分到这里。好的，那我们早点结束我们……

  * [19:39 - 19:56] **The Information Needs Template: Developing Intelligence Questions**
    And I'll do a simple exercise with you. Maybe I'll do it after I explain. Okay, can anyone tell what this tool is actually about? What this tool talks about? It's about coming up with a question. And you come up with a question collaboratively. That's why it is a tool. And in the process of coming up with that question that you're going to focus on for intelligence collaboratively, you also engage in the intelligence activity of gathering information. How do you go about doing it? Start from where?
    Let's assume that, or let's say that you're going to think of adopting a technology. One of you mentioned technology adoption, right? So here is the technology—that's the first step. You're going to come up with questions that would help you decide on whether you're going to adopt the technology in the organization or not, if that's the case. After the first step of identifying that technology, you're going to talk about **Application Areas**. What does that mean? What can the technology be used for? Where can the technology be used? And why would you do that?
    *Student:* Show market research. Where we can sell the technology.
    *Professor:* So this is more on the first case, right. If you're coming up with a new product, then what you're saying makes sense. If I'm coming up with the technology, if I were to invest in developing a technology, right, then you will talk about where the technology can be applied. Could it be applied in renewable energy sources? Could it be applied to autonomous vehicles? So you will start thinking like how **Dyson** thought: "The motor helps not just in a vacuum cleaner, it also helps in other products," etc. That's how you will think when you're coming up with a product, you know what I mean? But the context that we are talking about is adopting a technology *into* my organization. Then application areas would mean... the broader the application areas where the technology could be adopted and implemented, the more advantageous it is for me.
    Right? Because if there are two competing technologies: if one technology could be applied only in my marketing department and nowhere else, but the other technology could be applied for the marketing department, operational department, warehouse, logistics, whatnot—service sector, sales—wouldn't I bet on that technology better than the other technology? So when you are assessing such things itself, the decision maker would know: "Okay, this technology seems to be promising, more than the other one." Good idea. So intelligence automatically happens when there is a workshop happening with such tools.
    Narrowing down your search, and once the technology is picked and you start assessing where all it can be applied... Okay, if there are two technologies that a decision maker has in mind, the moment people say... that's why in **Kerr's** article, you have people from different departments. Why? Because it's a new technology. Someone from a different department will have a vision: "Oh, it could be applied in my department like this." They can voice it out, you see? So you have stakeholders from various groups brainstorming on where all the technology could be adopted. Or, "What all areas could a new technology which I am developing be utilized in?"—because they are my potential markets. You see, in the case of what Canton said, that is going to decide on the revenue that it will fetch once you do it.
    Then comes the part "above and below." You will start pondering about **Technological Aspects** on the lower bottom and **Market and Commercial Aspects** on the upper part. Let's discuss both contexts. If you're talking about adoption of a technology, what are technological or scientific questions that merit attention? Obvious, right? "How advanced is the technology?" "How revolutionary is the technology?" If it's too revolutionary, I have to revamp all my existing things to adopt a new technology that is destructive to my organization. What else?
    *Student:* What skills do I need to do?
    *Professor:* What skills do I need to [have]? It comes both here as well as there. If I'm a manager, if I were to adopt this, is my workforce skilled enough to adopt it or not? It's also a managerial question. What else?
    *Student:* The integration, the fit to the current company.
    *Professor:* That's what—how revolutionary it is. Would it fit my existing organizational setup and infrastructure or whatever?
    *Student:* You look at the cost to maintain the new product?
    *Professor:* Exactly. It comes under both technological and managerial. How expensive it is and can I afford it? Will I be able to see benefits of it as well, right? It comes under both blocks, but you need to separate it out. That is why you have people from different departments. Yes.
    *Student:* What is the readiness level of the technology?
    *Professor:* Exactly. Do I have the appetite? Remember the TRL (Technology Readiness Level) last week that we spoke about? Do I have the appetite or ability to adopt it? Let's give a chance to those who have never spoken in class. **Aishwarya** and **Amrita**, do you have anything to add?
    *Student:* If the customer will want it or not, any customer will need this technology.
    *Professor:* That will come for the second one which she mentioned. If I am developing the technology, I am assuming that all these are the application areas, but would my customers want it? Can they afford to buy it? That will be the other.
    *Student:* How much time it will take to...
    *Professor:* Very good. If it's a technology, it's going to take too long. Can I afford to wait that long? How long will it take to implement?
    *Student:* Does it have any ethical problems?
    *Professor:* Very nice. That's one of the problems which I had with the canvas and you rightly pointed out. While it talks about Technical and Management and Commercial, it does not stand up much for Ethical and Policy aspects as well. Very nice, thank you. Anything else? Anytime you talk about ethics, it will win my heart. I'm giving you the secret recipe for your logbook. But you need to use it wisely, okay? You cannot just go "blah blah blah" with ethics.
    So once you identify the context and identify the technology, you have a session of brainstorming to discuss the various technical, commercial, ethical, socio-political, policy-related questions. So once you have all these discussions happening, eventually they are narrowed down to a set of **Critical Questions** on which you're going to engage your analyst to work. From all these things, how would you arrive at this? Do you have to come to an agreement? These are very critical questions. If different stakeholders feel this is an important question, that automatically goes there. So it's not the boss—the boss is also there, but he collectively listens to people. Even in top-down, it could be consensual. You get input from various stakeholders to arrive at the questions which are critical for the organization. Now it becomes very focused. Now analysts know what they are going to work on.
    Right. Once this is done, it doesn't mean the workshop has ended and gone. They talk about *this* part. What is the second part? The second part is about: **"Identify local sources that should be watched. Identify distant sources that should be watched. Identify those sources that should be engaged."** This is very much similar to what we discussed. So when you have these decision makers from different departments together, you don't stop by just arriving at the right questions. Because these decision makers are senior officials who are well connected. Many times they can also act like scouts because of their networking. So when you arrive at those questions during the workshop, you also ask them: "Whom to watch and whom to talk to within and outside the industry?" And they will be giving bits and pieces of information which can be picked by the analysts for later on. So it kind of narrows down your search activities.
    I'll give you a very simple example of this—how critical this is. When NUS... let's take the example of **NUS** wanting to bet on either **Virtual Reality (VR)** technologies or **Artificial Intelligence (AI)**. Let's take this context, okay? Immediately you can see: of the two technologies, which one will have broader application areas? Virtual Reality or Artificial Intelligence? Artificial Intelligence, right? That has broader scope. If you look at VR, it's more like simulated experiments, labs, etc., training purposes and everything. But AI could have wider applications from all departments as well.
    Right now, when that was narrowed down, they started looking—this was a few years ago—they started looking at the technical aspects and whether we can adopt it. "How competent are we?" That's when, if you remember, you have been around for long. About 5 or 6 years ago there was a massive e-learning course which was thrown out on **IVLE**. We had IVLE at that point, not Canvas. It was a predecessor of Canvas that we have got. Everyone, all walks of NUS, they were asked to do data analysis courses. Faculty members, everybody, IT department. Massive e-learning course on upgrading our data analysis skills. So he used to call officials from there and give public lectures. Why? Because the other sources to watch were coming from "Big Shots." Because he travels extensively, he knows whom to watch or whom to talk to. And then the job of the analyst becomes a little easier because it is streamlined.
    So this is one way, if you were to conduct TI foresighting activities in your organization, how can you come up [with the questions]? Because if the question is wrong, everything goes wrong. Right. Whatever the right question... and not just talk, they also go one step further in terms of identifying sources, which makes your job easy.

    我来和你们做一个简单的练习。也许我解释完之后再做。好的，谁能告诉我这个工具到底是关于什么的？这个工具讲的是什么？它是关于提出一个问题的。而且是协作提出问题。这就是为什么它是一个工具。在这个协作提出你要专注于情报的那个问题的过程中，你也参与了收集信息的情报活动。你如何着手做这件事？从哪里开始？
    假设，或者说你要考虑采用一项技术。你们中有人提到了技术采用，对吧？所以这里有一项技术——这是第一步。你要提出有助于你决定是否在组织中采用该技术的问题（如果是这种情况的话）。在第一步确定了那项技术之后，你要讨论 **应用领域（Application Areas）**。那意味着什么？这项技术可以用来做什么？这项技术可以用在哪里？你为什么要那样做？
    *学生：* 展示市场研究。我们可以在哪里销售这项技术。
    *教授：* 这更多是针对第一种情况，对。如果你是在推出一个新产品，那你说的有道理。如果我是提出一项技术，如果我要投资开发一项技术，对，那么你会谈论这项技术可以应用在哪里。它能应用在可再生能源领域吗？能应用在自动驾驶汽车上吗？所以你会开始像 **Dyson（戴森）** 那样思考：“电机不仅有助于吸尘器，还有助于其他产品，”等等。当你推出一个产品时，你会那样思考，你懂我的意思吗？但我们正在谈论的背景是将一项技术 *采用* 到我的组织中。那么应用领域就意味着……这项技术可以被采用和实施的应用领域越广，对我来说就越有利。
    对吗？因为如果有两项竞争技术：如果一项技术只能应用在我的营销部门，其他任何地方都不行；但另一项技术可以应用在营销部门、运营部门、仓库、物流、不管什么——服务部门、销售——我难道不会押注在那项技术上，而不是另一项吗？所以当你评估这些事情本身时，决策者就会知道：“好的，这项技术似乎比另一项更有前途。”好主意。所以当使用这样的工具进行研讨会时，情报活动会自动发生。
    缩小你的搜索范围，一旦选中了技术，你就开始评估它可以应用的所有地方……好的，如果决策者心中有两项技术，当人们说……这就是为什么在 **Kerr** 的文章中，你会让来自不同部门的人参与。为什么？因为这是一项新技术。来自不同部门的人会有愿景：“噢，它可以像这样应用在我的部门。”他们可以说出来，你看？所以你有来自不同群体的利益相关者进行头脑风暴，讨论这项技术可以被采用的所有地方。或者，“我正在开发的这项新技术可以在哪些领域被利用？”——因为它们是我的潜在市场。你看，就 Canton 所说的而言，一旦你做了，这将决定它将带来的收入。
    然后是“上面和下面”的部分。你会开始思考底部的 **技术方面** 和上部的 **市场与商业方面**。让我们讨论这两种背景。如果你在谈论采用一项技术，哪些技术或科学问题值得关注？很明显，对吧？“这项技术有多先进？”“这项技术有多具革命性？”如果它太具革命性，我必须彻底改造我现有的所有东西来采用一项对我组织具有破坏性的新技术。还有什么？
    *学生：* 我需要做什么技能？
    *教授：* 我需要[拥有]什么技能？这既涉及到这里也涉及到那里。如果我是经理，如果我要采用这个，我的员工是否有足够的技能来采用它？这也是一个管理问题。还有什么？
    *学生：* 整合，与当前公司的契合度。
    *教授：* 就是那个——它有多具革命性。它是否适合我现有的组织设置和基础设施或者其他什么？
    *学生：* 你看维护新产品的成本？
    *教授：* 没错。它既属于技术也属于管理。它有多贵，我能负担得起吗？我也能看到它的好处吗，对吧？它属于两个模块，但你需要把它分开。这就是为什么你有来自不同部门的人。是的。
    *学生：* 技术的就绪水平是什么？
    *教授：* 没错。我有胃口吗？还记得我们上周讲的 TRL（技术就绪指数）吗？我有胃口或能力采用它吗？让我们给那些从未在课堂上发过言的人一个机会。**Aishwarya** 和 **Amrita**，你们有什么要补充的吗？
    *学生：* 客户是否想要它，是否有客户需要这项技术。
    *教授：* 那会属于她提到的第二个问题。如果我在开发技术，我假设所有这些都是应用领域，但我的客户会想要它吗？他们买得起吗？那将是另一个问题。
    *学生：* 需要多长时间才能……
    *教授：* 很好。如果是技术，它需要太长时间。我能等那么久吗？实施需要多长时间？
    *学生：* 它有任何伦理问题吗？
    *教授：* 非常好。那是我对这个画布（Canvas）有的问题之一，你正确地指出了。虽然它谈论了技术、管理和商业，但它在伦理和政策方面并没有体现太多。非常好，谢谢你。还有别的吗？任何时候你谈论伦理，都会赢得我的心。我在给你们 Logbook 的秘方。但你需要明智地使用它，好吗？你不能只是关于伦理“巴拉巴拉”一通。
    所以一旦你确定了背景并确定了技术，你就要进行头脑风暴会议，讨论各种技术、商业、伦理、社会政治、政策相关的问题。所以一旦你有所有这些讨论发生，最终它们会被缩小到一组 **关键问题（Critical Questions）**，你将让你的分析师针对这些问题工作。从所有这些事情中，你如何得出这个？你必须达成一致吗？这些是非常关键的问题。如果不同的利益相关者觉得这是一个重要问题，那它会自动进入那里。所以不是老板——老板也在那里，但他集体听取人们的意见。即使在自上而下的模式中，它也可以是共识性的。你从各种利益相关者那里获得输入，以得出对组织至关重要的问题。现在它变得非常聚焦。现在分析师知道他们要研究什么了。
    对。一旦这完成了，并不意味着研讨会就结束了。他们会谈论 *这* 部分。第二部分是关于：**“确定应该关注的本地来源。确定应该关注的远程来源。确定应该接触的来源。”** 这与我们讨论的非常相似。所以当你有这些来自不同部门的决策者在一起时，你不会止步于仅仅得出正确的问题。因为这些决策者是人脉广泛的高级官员。很多时候，由于他们的人脉网络，他们也可以充当侦察员。所以当你在研讨会上得出这些问题时，你也问他们：“在行业内外应该关注谁，应该和谁交谈？”他们会给出零碎的信息，分析师可以在以后通过评论拾取这些信息。所以这在某种程度上缩小了你的搜索活动。
    我给你们一个非常简单的例子——这有多关键。当 **NUS**……让我们以 NUS 想要押注 **虚拟现实（VR）** 技术还是 **人工智能（AI）** 为例。让我们以此为背景，好吗？立刻你可以看到：在这两项技术中，哪一项会有更广泛的应用领域？虚拟现实还是人工智能？人工智能，对吧？那个有更广泛的范围。如果你看 VR，它更像是模拟实验、实验室等，培训目的和一切。但 AI 可以有更广泛的应用，来自所有部门。
    现在，当那个被缩小范围后，他们开始看——这是几年前的事了——他们开始看技术方面以及我们是否能采用它。“我们有多大能力？”就在那时，如果你还记得，如果你在这里待得够久。大约 5 或 6 年前，有一个大规模的电子学习课程在 **IVLE** 上推出。那时我们用的是 IVLE，不是 Canvas。它是我们现在拥有的 Canvas 的前身。每个人，NUS 的各行各业，都被要求做数据分析课程。教职员工，每个人，IT 部门。大规模的电子学习课程，提升我们的数据分析技能。然后当官员——在那时是 **Tan Eng Chye（陈永财）**，对吧？——所以当他过去高度评价中国保险行业的这些公司时，甚至不是教育行业的，它们大量使用 AI 作为战略优势。所以他过去常给那里的官员打电话，并做公开讲座。为什么？因为其他要关注的来源来自“大人物”。因为他经常出差，他知道该关注谁或该和谁交谈。然后分析师的工作变得稍微容易一些，因为它是流水线化的。
    所以这是一种方法，如果你要在你的组织中进行 TI 预见活动，你如何提出[问题]？因为如果问题错了，一切都错了。对。无论什么是正确的问题……不仅是谈论，他们还在确定来源方面更进一步，这让你的工作变得容易。
    所以回到第一天的活动：如果你被聘为分析师，你会做什么？你会做的第一步是什么？还记得第一周吗？给他打电话。来这里，也邀请我。还有你。和你的朋友们，每个人，对吧？还有邻居和每个人。所以那就是你要做的——基础设施人员——然后开始做这个练习。提出你要获取数据的问题。非常简单的工具，对吧？
    我曾经讨厌我的老板，当时他问我，“嘿，来吧，做这个模块，”你知道吗？我说，“噢，这是……这门课没头没尾的。我怎么教这个？”然后花了好几年去……他们和人交谈。这就是为什么我有这么多客座讲座，因为他们每个人都是各自领域的专家，收集零碎信息并将它们放入一个连贯的框架中。这不是开玩笑，但我现在爱死他让我做这个了。因为这门课很多学校都没有开设。**剑桥（Cambridge）** 是这方面的地方。而且他们，你知道，这个工具也是来自剑桥。是的，是的。顺便说一句，如果你想使用这些工具中的任何一个，我可以和那些人谈谈，因为……另外他们在 COVID 期间做了这个。以前一切都是以……的形式，你知道当 **Rob Phaal** 进行研发路线图绘制（R&D mapping）时，他的纸会是那张大纸，官员们在上面贴便利贴。这就是他在新加坡进行研发路线图绘制的方式。我见过他那样做，所有这些工具都那么大。但当 COVID 爆发时，一切都迅速数字化了。一切都以数字形式发生。是的，所以有些工具代表……现成可用的。他给我和这门课的学生提供了访问权限。如果你想为你自己的组织使用它，他会做一个客座讲座。
  * [19:56 - 20:16] **Organizational Structures for Intelligence: Structured, Informal, Hybrid**
    Okay, now coming back to the framework. Next important topic is **Structure**. What structure? This comes from various articles which are in the reading list. I said don't have to read it because they're not easy to read. That is why I said don't shield it. What is structure? Structure is: how are you going to plan, structure the intelligence activities? How the various people are going to be disposed in an organization? What kind of mode do you need to adopt? And typically there are three structures floating around. One is **Structured Approach** (Centralized). The other one is the **Informal Approach** (Decentralized). Third one is the **Hybrid Approach**. Nothing rocket science. It's something we discussed. It's very similar to the top-down, bottom-up approach.
    **Structured Approach** is where there is a **Central TI Unit** (Intelligence Unit), which is typically located at the headquarters. And they will have analysts, they will have key people there. And to help them, there will be **Decentralized TI Units**. There are quite a few in Singapore as decentralized units because [they want] to tap into the Asian region intelligence. And apart from that, they also have all these people to help them. What are these people? It could be VC funding. Since you spoke about VC, it could be that there is a Venture Capital fund department in the company which is given some resource. What is the use of that unit for Intelligence? They will go and look for what is the latest... see from those, and if it becomes promising, bring in-house. They are also part of the intelligence unit.
    And **Post-docs and Sabbaticals**. There is one article which I have given on **Kodak**. This company doesn't exist now [in the same form]. At that point they were very smart in intelligence but they got disrupted because of technological [change]. And one of the ways when they were expanding to different regions was to have interns/post-docs. They used to ask them: if they're expanding into a region, they would have post-docs from that region to go and ask, "Who is the top-notch researcher in that place whom I can collaborate with? Which funding agency is good?" So they also become part of your intelligence, just that they're all outsiders. Most of these people are insiders.
    They have **Technology Envoys** or typical **Listening Posts**. These are people who are parked in different locations for the company not to do much of a job other than listening and gathering information and passing it on. Also have **Expert Collectors**, that's what I told about the pharmaceutical industry. No company is hiring one consultant meeting in the airport; they're all part of the expert networks. And then lead suppliers, sometimes customers, they are also your intelligence agents; they give information as well. So what they do is, while all the decision making is done at headquarters—it's very top-down—if some intelligence needs to be sought from Asia, they would pass the question to these units or they try to mobilize anyone of those to get the information. And then they collect the information from these decentralized stores and they give it to the decision maker. They take the decision and it's passed off to various entities. It's very structured. Very hierarchical.
    Now, what is **Informal Structure**? Informal structure is what you all talked about wherein everyone becomes an intelligence agent, right? Everyone does the job. And there might be a central intelligence unit, but their job is more like **establishing communication routines and reward mechanisms**. Ensure that you have proper incentives. For example, there is **Slack Resources** in place which I mentioned—giving employees freedom, slack time for them to work on intelligence sources. Have communication strategies, knowledge management structures, infrastructure for **Communities of Practice**. This is knowledge management: people get together and talk about ideas. Incentives. Reward mechanisms. **Job Rotation**. Why do you have job rotation? You enable these things. Your job is to enable all these things happening so that someone said, right, "We all become knowledge workers, we gather information and then we pass it on." For that to happen, you have all these mechanisms. What is the purpose of job rotation?
    *Student:* First, transfer the knowledge. Secondly, you can improve the process by addressing the gap.
    *Professor:* Address cross-pollination of ideas. Understand... you know one of you mentioned about "this person did not understand, couldn't be integrated." And in fact in many good organizations that I know of, you will not be able to climb up the ladder unless you have been exposed to different functional areas in the company and also different regions as well. Okay, there are companies that anyone undergoing that... you will be put into different functional areas.
    One of my... I had a master student, she was a very smart student from the **Philippines**. She was an ASEAN scholar who came to do a master's program and she was hired by one of the companies—a good company, a consulting company—and she was put into different, you know, job roles: operational, sometimes in the warehouse, sometimes the marketing department, and she was made to travel around the world. And it's only after that you will be able to climb up the ladder. Otherwise you're done. If you leave the organization, you cannot reach the benefits out of it. That is when you know you become a better knowledge worker to add to the organization. That's what they do. This is Informal. So the job of central unit is to ensure that every mechanism is put in place for it to function smoothly, enable that the information flows up. Enable that employees are pumped up to work on [it]. Enable that latest cross-pollination of ideas.
    Now what is **Hybrid**? It can happen this way as well with central unit delegating the job. But in some situations, let's say you know what happened in a pharmaceutical company again, is that when this **Combinatorial Chemistry** came about? They thought, "Okay, this is going to be disruptive," so they formed a group of people. They started forming a **Community of Practice** on this topic, combinatorial chemistry, to understand more about it. And then when enough interest and momentum gathered, it became a separate intelligence unit on its own. Okay. And once it matured, it was integrated back to the central unit. So it's like informal groups created, but once it became matured and became important, sometimes the informal group will decide that "Okay, this is not going to help," so let's ditch it. That also happens. But if it becomes something solid and important, it gets integrated into the Central Intelligence Unit.
    So now the question is: **Which structure to adopt?** Goes back to the same thing in reality. There are organizations which adopt only a single mode approach wherein we take either structured approach or informal approach. But there are organizations which adopt multi-role approaches. Okay, which means all three approaches together. They might be central structure, but it's more like they have informal as well. Both work together and it all depends on the company culture and decision making style—whether it's centralized, decentralized or how entrepreneurial is the company culture. And what this chart says is how different industries either go with one mode or multi-mode. The latest industries are all in here. They will go with multi-modes having a more entrepreneurial culture.
    Okay. So what structure is there in your company? You don't have one? Are you doing this more informal? Meredith, so what is your thing?

Many times the focus group remains discussion. It stops there. But does it go up? That defines whether it is working or not.     I don't know if I mentioned this to my other class last semester. You know the **Colgate** company, right? That makes toothpaste. Let me try to remember this example. Okay.     But the idea which was implemented was from a security [guard]... he was at the gate, you know, a security of the organization.     Now. So what do the cases talk about? Firms can have multiple structures at the same time. The kind of structure they adopt and how effective it is will depend on a lot of contextual factors. Depends on culture. How centralized or decentralized? One of the reward mechanisms are these **Slack Resources**. Slack resource is a big research topic. If an organization is not giving slack resources, you can't do informal intelligence, right? What are slack resources? Apart from your day-to-day job, you have some pocket of money for doing these exploratory activities. We do have what is called **STAR Grant**, which our department gives every now and then that we can use it to pay for research assistants, exploratory projects and everything. Nothing more. Okay.
    好的，现在回到框架。下一个重要的话题是 **结构（Structure）**。什么结构？这来自阅读清单中的各种文章。我说过不必读，因为它们不容易读。这就是为什么我说不要回避它。什么是结构？结构是：你打算如何规划、构建情报活动？各种人员在组织中如何配置？你需要采用什么样的模式？通常有三种结构在流传。一种是 **结构化方法（Structured Approach，集中式）**。另一种是 **非正式方法（Informal Approach，分散式）**。第三种是 **混合方法（Hybrid Approach）**。没什么深奥的。这是我们讨论过的东西。这与自上而下、自下而上的方法非常相似。
    **结构化方法** 是指有一个 **中央 TI 单元（Central TI Unit）**（情报单元），通常位于总部。他们会有分析师，那里会有关键人员。为了帮助他们，会有 **分散的 TI 单元**。在新加坡有不少分散的单元，因为[他们想]利用亚洲地区的情报。除此之外，他们还有所有这些人来帮助他们。这些人是什么？可能是风投（VC）资金。既然你提到了风投，可能是公司里有一个风险投资基金部门，被给予了一些资源。那个单元对情报有什么用？他们会去寻找最新的……从那些里面看，如果变得有前途，就引入内部。他们也是情报单元的一部分。
    还有 **博士后和休假人员**。我给过一篇关于 **Kodak（柯达）** 的文章。这家公司现在不存在了[以同样的形式]。在那时他们在情报方面非常聪明，但因为技术[变革]而被颠覆了。当他们向不同地区扩张时，方法之一就是拥有实习生/博士后。他们过去常问他们：如果他们要扩张到一个地区，他们会让那个地区的博士后去问，“那个地方谁是顶尖的研究人员，我可以和谁合作？哪个资助机构好？”所以他们也成了你情报的一部分，只是他们都是外人。这些大多数人是内部人员。
    他们有 **技术特使（Technology Envoys）** 或典型的 **监听站（Listening Posts）**。这些人被安置在公司的不同地点，除了倾听和收集信息并传递之外，不做太多工作。还有 **专家收集者（Expert Collectors）**，那就是我讲过的制药行业。没有公司是雇佣一个顾问在机场开会的；他们都是专家网络的一部分。然后主要供应商，有时是客户，他们也是你的情报代理人；他们也提供信息。所以他们做的是，虽然所有的决策都在总部完成——这是非常自上而下的——如果需要从亚洲寻求一些情报，他们会把问题传递给这些单元，或者试图动员其中任何一个来获取信息。然后他们从这些分散的存储中收集信息，交给决策者。他们做决定，然后传递给各个实体。这是非常结构化的。非常等级森严。
    现在，什么是 **非正式结构**？非正式结构就是你们都谈到的，每个人都成为情报代理人，对吧？每个人都做这份工作。可能会有一个中央情报单元，但他们的工作更像是 **建立沟通程序和奖励机制**。确保你有适当的激励措施。例如，有适当的 **松弛资源（Slack Resources）**，这是我提到的——给员工自由，给他们松弛时间去研究情报来源。有沟通策略，知识管理结构，**实践社区（Communities of Practice）** 的基础设施。这就是知识管理：人们聚在一起谈论想法。激励措施。奖励机制。**工作轮换（Job Rotation）**。为什么要有工作轮换？你启用这些事情。你的工作是促成所有这些事情发生，以便有人说的，对，“我们都成为知识工作者，我们收集信息然后传递它。”为了发生这种情况，你有所有这些机制。工作轮换的目的是什么？
    *学生：* 首先，转移知识。其次，你可以通过解决差距来改进流程。
    *教授：* 解决思想的交叉授粉。理解……你们中有人提到“这个人不理解，无法整合。”事实上，在我知道的许多好公司里，除非你接触过公司里的不同职能领域以及不同地区，否则你无法晋升。好的，有些公司，任何经历过那个的人……你会被放到不同的职能领域。
    我的一个……我有一个硕士生，她是来自 **菲律宾** 的非常聪明的学生。她是一名来读硕士项目的东盟学者，她被其中一家公司雇佣了——一家好公司，一家咨询公司——她被放到不同的，你知道，工作角色中：运营，有时在仓库，有时在营销部门，她被安排在世界各地旅行。只有在那之后你才能晋升。否则你就完了。如果你离开组织，你就无法从中获得好处。那就是你知道你成为一个更好的知识工作者来为组织增值的时候。那就是他们做的。这是非正式的。所以中央单元的工作是确保每一个机制都到位以使其平稳运行，促使信息向上流动。促使员工有动力去工作。促使最新的思想交叉授粉。
    现在什么是 **混合结构**？也可以这样发生，中央单元委派工作。但在某些情况下，比方说你知道在一家制药公司又发生了什么，就是当 **组合化学（Combinatorial Chemistry）** 出现时？他们想，“好的，这将是颠覆性的，”所以他们组成了一群人。他们开始就这个话题，组合化学，形成一个 **实践社区**，以了解更多。然后当聚集了足够的兴趣和势头时，它变成了一个独立的、自成一体的情报单元。好的。一旦它成熟了，它就被重新整合回中央单元。所以这就像创建了非正式小组，但一旦它成熟并变得重要，有时非正式小组会决定“好的，这没有帮助，”所以让我们放弃它。那也会发生。但如果它变成了某种坚实而重要的东西，它就会被整合进中央情报单元。
    所以现在的问题是：**采用哪种结构？** 在现实中回到同样的事情。有些组织只采用单一模式方法，即我们要么采取结构化方法，要么采取非正式方法。但也有组织采用多角色方法。好的，这意味着所有三种方法一起。他们可能有中央结构，但更像是他们也有非正式的。两者一起工作，这完全取决于公司文化和决策风格——是集中的、分散的，还是公司文化有多具创业精神。这张图表说的是不同的行业如何要么采用单一模式，要么采用多模式。最新的行业都在这里。他们会采用多模式，拥有更具创业精神的文化。
    好的。那么你们公司是什么结构？你们没有？你们做得更非正式吗？Meredith，你的情况呢？
    *学生（Meredith）：* 结构化的。
    *教授：* 结构化的。来自新加坡政府机构，对吧？非常非常结构化。或者是临时组建的？这就是为什么结构化方法会行得通。你看，这在新加坡发生过，当研发规划发生时……在此之前他们通常……你知道 **Yeoh Keat Chuan（杨吉全）**（EDB 董事总经理）吗？他是一个创造者。在决定支柱产业之前，新加坡邀请来自世界各地的顶尖研究人员聚集在那里，决定专注于什么支柱产业。申请研究拨款。所以那是一个非常有趣的过程。我碰巧见证了一次。那就是我给另一个基金打电话的时候。我在向他们做演示，那时我拿到了 **天然气水合物（Gas Hydrates）** 研究的资金。是的，安全部门。哪种结构？我会叫你“班级安全员”。
    *学生：* 结构化的。所以在总部有……
    *教授：* 非常像这样结构化的。单元的智能，对吧？他们是单元真正的智能。这甚至发生在，你知道，当我们讲知识管理时。我会谈论一件你们可能都知道的事，很多人在国民服役（NS）时可能也做过：**行动后回顾（After Action Review）**。这是一个结构化的情报小组，实际上非常对。它全都来自军队，是的。
    *学生：* 我对此有一个问题。你也提到了像中小企业（SME）。我认为这是非常非正式的事情，但我有一个问题，因为在我看来：一旦你从中小企业往上爬，扩大规模成为大型、巨型企业——像你说政府公司是大型企业——中小企业处于非正式[结构]更好吗？还是中小企业可以是结构化的？或者是等级制的……这是效果最好的？大公司是结构化的效果最好，还是大公司也可以是非正式的？
    *教授：* 是的，我给你们看的大公司，很多都是非正式的。所以情况不一定如此。不仅仅是规模的问题。也是文化的问题。你知道 **Google**，对吧？所以不[仅仅是规模]。但话虽如此，中小企业能负担得起的只有非正式的。他们养不起一群……他们在新加坡甚至养不起研发人员。那就是他们看到的。然后只有情报人员，对。所以话虽如此，这就是为什么他们想从一个非常没有预见的状态转变。当他们试图适应那种结构化方法带来的预见好处时，通过获得 **A*STAR（新科研）** 的许可。以及这些项目，所有这些有技术顾问与 A*STAR 一起进行绘图活动的。所以他们试图通过依靠“老大哥”来获得结构化方法的好处。但除此之外，非正式是他们能负担得起的。但这对于中小企业来说变得更容易。为什么？因为沟通流动很容易。很好。还有什么你可以问 **Vinod**，当他来的时候？他在大公司工作过，然后他有自己的初创公司。我们会谈论研发绘图和……
    *学生：* 我不敢相信你们不做非正式情报……这在每个组织都会发生，但问题是你们是否正在……

    但被实施的想法来自一个保安……他在大门口，你知道，组织的一个保安。他给出了这个主意：**“只要把牙膏口稍微增大一点。”** 所以如果孔稍微变大，会发生什么？更多的牙膏被挤出来。这个来自保安的主意是如此该死的简单，它被实施了。那是最大的部分，对吧？它被实施以增加销售，而且它奏效了。难怪现在我们有不同尺寸的，对吧？小的，大的，你知道，但有时即使对于小管，孔也是大的。所以那来自某人的情报，你可能不会轻易想到。那就是一种组织文化——听取任何人的意见并实施。
    现在。所以案例说明了什么？公司可以同时拥有多种结构。他们采用什么样的结构以及它有多有效将取决于许多背景因素。取决于文化。是集中式还是分散式？奖励机制之一是这些 **松弛资源（Slack Resources）**。松弛资源是一个很大的研究课题。如果一个组织不给松弛资源，你就不能做非正式情报，对吧？什么是松弛资源？除了你的日常工作，你有一些钱袋子用于做这些探索性活动。我们确实有所谓的 **STAR Grant**，我们系时不时会给，我们可以用它来支付研究助理、探索性项目等等。他们不限制你必须如何使用它。当然有因为我们在新加坡 NUS 的限制。但它仍然是开放的，不像严格的课程。然后公司在地理上如何分布——这也决定了不同结构的有效性，有效的沟通。以及行业特定的。早些时候我们在之前的图表中看到，机械类那种非常传统的行业更多偏向这一边——结构化方法。而新兴行业更多在右边。仅此而已。好的。

# Readings
## Week 2
  Corporate Foresight Benchmarking Report by Rene Rohrbeck
  1. What is the purpose of the benchmarking report?
  2. List down the challenges outlined by the authors in establishing the impact of corporate foresight?
  3. How did the authors address each one of those challenges?
  4. How many items were there in measuring Corporate Foresight Need and Corporate Foresight Maturity? What are they (no need to list each one of those, just list the dimensions)?
  5. How did they measure performance?
  6. Why should you give importance to aspects in Questions 2-5?
  7. On the basis of corporate foresight need and maturity, how did they categorize the firms based on their corporate foresighting profile?
  8. What are the three core skills of vigilant firms? What are they? Can you highlight examples of activities related to the three core skills?
  9. Why firms find it difficult to engage in corporate foresighting activities?
  10. How to address the challenges that prevent firms from engaging in foresighting activities?

# Discussion
## Week 4
  During my time as an Algorithm Engineer, our Technology Intelligence (TI) activities mainly focused on **Targeting and Scanning**. This includes many kinds of SOTA architectures we can provide toour customers, like recent LLM models, Stable Diffusion and acceleration techniques (e.g., quantization, speculative decoding).

  **How we captured impact:**
  We focused on **technical performance metrics** firstly,instead of direct economic valuation in the short term. For achieving this, We used strict technical benchmarks. For example, when porting a PyTorch model to our inference framework, the KPIs were **inference latency** (ms), **throughput** (tokens/sec), and **accuracy retention** (ensuring loss < 1% after quantization). In the long-term, the value was actually valued by the **enablement of hardware ecosystems**. By successfully optimizing these models, we ensured our hardware remained competitive against our competitors.

  **Who conducted the assessment:**
  We have a team, which is normally 2-3 people, specifically investigating new technologies, and validated by out project leaders or higher level discussion meetings. So it's both a bottom-up and top-down process.

  **Suggestions for Improvement:**
  While our technical KPIs were precise, we lacked a direct link to **economic KPIs** during the R&D phase. Sometimes we need to go to customers' site for further debugging of their issues, and it could be a better opportunity for understanding their pain points, but it's not very frequently.
  An improvement would be talk and hear directly from customers, This would help engineering teams better visualize the business value of the intelligence activity beyond just "beating the benchmark."

***

# Syllabus
## Course Description
  Successful R&D engineers and managers should have the foresight to anticipate and drive technological changes and convert them into strategic assets to organizations. This course will equip students with technology forecasting, intelligence and foresighting skills, make use of the foresight to generate strategic intellectual assets and realize value from them to succeed in competitive environment. Effective collection and transformation of information into intelligence requires awareness of enterprise niches and alternatives, as well as the search and analytical skills of data and information. The course will emphasize these skills and impart a thorough understanding business & technology related strategic frameworks.
## Welcome to the course!
  Welcome to MT5010!

  I am Annapoornima Subramanian, lecturer for MT5010 for this semester.

  We all know that organizations need to develop insights into future alternatives and be relevant in order to enjoy sustained competitive advantage. Doing so is more critical for R&D intensive organizations as firms in high-technology industries are constantly threatened with technological discontinuities. Therefore, this module aims to equip students with strategic insights and analytical skills of technology forecasting & intelligence that are essential for high-tech companies to survive in a transient and competitive environment. Effective technological intelligence and forecasting requires a comprehensive awareness of enterprise niches and alternatives, analytical skills of data/information, knowledge management and considerations to organizational structures. Hence, this module covers range of topics including technology intelligence (a) mission (b) structure (c) processes, (d) management, and (e) tools.  Thus, apart from introducing the theory and practice of technology forecasting & intelligence, the module will provide hands-on training on technology intelligence and forecasting tools.
## Grading Components & Details
  The grading requirement involves both individual and group work. Individual work includes class participation, and a logbook submission. Group work includes a group project (either of a company of your choice or Straumann/NRP cases provided in Canvas).

  The breakdown of grading components is as follows

  Grading

  Individual Component (60%)

  Class Participation 30%
  Logbook  (26 April, 9pm) 30%
  Group Component (40%)
  Group Project or Straumann case or Singapore's NRP (15 April) 40%                                     
  Description

  Individual Component

  Class Participation (30% grade): Students are expected to analyze the readings and cases and contribute to class discussion. You are graded on quality rather than quantity. I will be inviting many guest lecturers for this module. Asking interesting questions during the guest lectures is a way to improve your class participation score.

  Logbook (30% grade): Throughout the semester, I will assign articles for discussion in each class and facilitate group activities. You are required to maintain a logbook that documents the discussion components from each session. Students who have taken MT5007 may already be familiar with this requirement; for those who haven't, I will provide a detailed briefing during the first lecture.

  Your logbook should focus on capturing the key discussion points from each class and connecting these insights to real-world applications. You need to cover a maximum of five topics in your logbook. The submission deadline is April 26, 2026.

  Group Component

  Group Project (40% grade)  Students are expected to form groups by themselves. Groups are expected to make a presentation and it can take one of the following two forms. Please note that there is no need to submit report. Just presentation is enough and slides are to be submitted to Canvas. Each group will have to make a presentation for 15-18 mins. This will be followed by Q&A for 2 mins.

  Technology Intelligence practices in your organization/If you were to initiate Technology Intelligence activities in your organization, how would you go about structuring and executing them.
  Presentation on Technological Intelligence Activities in a SME called Straumann. This case is published in a book. Groups need to understand the TI journey of Straumann and present their critical analysis of the same.
  Presentation on the Strategic foresight activities of Singapore’s National Robotics Programme (NRP). This case is published in a book. Groups need to understand the journey of Strategic Foresight Journey of NRP Singapore and present their critical analysis of the same.

  In the second half of the module, we will focus on technology intelligence methods such as Delphi Method, Trend Analysis, S-Curve Analysis, Bibliometric Analysis, Roadmapping, Technology Radar.
